كما في صبي أُودع عبداً فقتله، فإن أتلف مالاً بلا إيداع ضمن، وإن أتلف بعده لا وجه الاستحسان: أنه لا يضمن بالغصب، بل بالإتلاف تسبيبا بنقله إلى مكان فيه الصواعق أو الحيات. (كما في صبي) أودع عبداً فقتله، فإن أتلف مالاً بلا إيداع ضَمِن، وإن أتلف بعده لا الإيداع يتعدى إلى المفعولين، يقال: أودعت زيداً درهماً، فالفعل المجهول وهو أودع، أسند إلى المفعول الأول وهو الصبي، فالوديعة عنده إن كان [١] قوله: إلى مكان فيه للصواعق أو الحيات؛ وهذا لأنَّ الصواعق والحيات والسباع لا تكون في كل مكان، فأمكن حفظه عنه، فإذا نقله إليه وهو متعد في ذلك النقل، وقد أزال حفظ الولي فيضاف إليه؛ لأن شرط العلة ينزل منزلة العلة إذا كان تعدياً كالحفر في الطريق. بخلاف الموتِ فجأة، أو بحمى؛ لأنّ ذلك لا يختلف باختلاف الأمكنة، حتى لو نقله إلى موضع يغلب فيه الحمى والأمراض، نقول بأنه يضمن فتجبُ الدِّية على عاقلة الغاصب؛ لكونه قتلا تسبيبا. هكذا في «الهداية»).
[٢] قوله: كما في صبي... الخ؛ أي تضمن عاقلة الغاصب كمـا يضمن عاقلة الصبي إذا قتل العبد المودع عنده، ولا يضمن إن أتلف الصبي المال المودع عنده. وهاهنا احتمالات أربعة؛ لأنّ الشيء المتلف إمّا مودع عند الصبي أو غير مودع، وهذا الشيء إما عبد أو غيره، ولم يذكر المصنف الله حكم العبد الغير المودع لظهوره وهو الضمان، والفرق بين العبد المودع والمال المودع عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. قال أبو يوسف والشافعي له: يضمن الصبي المودع في الوجهين، وعلى هذا لو أودع العبد المحجور عليه مالاً فاستهلكه الصبي، لا يؤخذ بالضمان في الحال عند أبي حنيفة، ويؤخذ بـه بعـد العتق، وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي له يؤخذ في الحال، وعلى هذا الخلافِ الإقرار في العبد والصبي، وكذا الإعادة فيهما، ثم إن محمداً لله شرط في «الجامع الصغير أن يكون الصبي عاقلاً. وفي «الجامع الكبير» وضع المسألة في الصبي الذي عمره اثني عشر سنة، وذلك
حسن الدراية لأواخر شرح الوقاية
[۱]
عبداً ضمنه بالقتل، وإن كان مالاً غيرَهُ لا يضمنه عند أبي حنيفة له ومحمد له، ويضمن عند أبي يوسف والشافعي الله؛ لأنه أتلف مالا معصوماً. قلنا: غير العبد معصوم لحق السيد، وقد فوته حيث وضعَهُ في يد الصبي، وأما العبد فعصمتُهُ لحقه إذ هو مبقى على أصل الحرية في حق الدم. دليل على أن غير العاقل يضمن بالاتفاق؛ ولأنّ التسليط غير معتبر فيه، وفعله معتبر. كذا في «التكملة»).
[١] قوله: ضمنه بالقتل؛ أي صارت دية على عاقلة الصبي بالإجماع. كذا في الجلبي»
[٢] قوله: لأنه أتلف مالاً؛ أي متقوّماً معصوماً حقاً للمالك، فيجب عليه ضمانه، كما إذا كانت الوديعة عبداً، أو كان الصبي مأذوناً له في التجارة أو في الحفظ من جهة الولي، وكذا إذا أتلف غير ما في يده، ولم يكن معصوماً؛ لثبوت ولاية الاستهلاك فيه. [٣] قوله: قلنا؛ توضيحه: إنّ الصبي أتلف مالاً غير معصوم، فلا يؤاخذ بضمانه، كما لو أتلفه بإذنه ورضاه؛ وهذا لأنّ العصمة تثبت حقاً له، وقد فوتها على نفسه، حيث وضعه في يد غير مانعة، فلا يبقى معصوماً إلا إذا أقام غيره مقام نفسه في الحفظ، ولا إقامة هاهنا؛ لأنه لا ولاية له على الصبي حتى يلزمه، ولا ولاية للصبي على نفسه، حتى يلتزم بخلافِ المأذون له؛ لأنّ له ولاية على نفسه كالبالغ. وبخلاف ما إذا كانت الوديعة عبداً؛ لأنّ عصمته لحق نفسه، أو هو مبقى على أصل الحرية في حق الأم، فكانت عصمتُه لحقِّ نفسه لا للمالك؛ لأنّ عصمة المالك إنما تعتبر فيما له ولاية استهلاك، حتى يمكن غيره من الاستهلاكِ بالتسليط، وليس للمولى ولاية استهلاك عبده، فلا يقدر أن يمكّن غيره من ذلك، فلا يعتبر تسليطه، فيضمن الصبي باستهلاكه بخلاف سائر الأموال.
The book of blood money / its types and rulings. As in a minor who was entrusted with a slave and killed him: if he destroys property without deposit, he guarantees; and if he destroys after that, there is no [liability]. The basis of istihsan: he does not guarantee due to usurpation, but due to destruction by causation by moving it to a place containing thunderbolts or snakes. (As in a minor) who was entrusted with a slave and killed him; if he destroys property without deposit, he guarantees; and if he destroys after that, no. The verb 'deposit' (awda'a) is transitive to two objects: one says 'I deposited a dirham with Zayd'. The passive verb 'awdi'a' is attributed to the first object, which is the minor. So the deposit with him is... [1] His statement: 'to a place containing thunderbolts or snakes'; this is because thunderbolts, snakes, and predators are not in every place, so it is possible to protect [the property] from them. So when he moves it there, he is transgressing in that movement, and he has removed the guardian's protection, so it is attributed to him; because the condition for the cause takes the place of the cause if it is transgressive, like digging a road. Unlike sudden death or fever; because that does not differ according to places; so if he moves it to a place where fever and diseases prevail, we say he guarantees, so the blood money is due on the 'āqila of the usurper because it is homicide by causation. Thus in al-Hidāyah. [2] His statement: 'as in a minor...' i.e., the 'āqila of the usurper guarantees just as the 'āqila of the minor guarantees if he kills the deposited slave, and he does not guarantee if the minor destroys the property deposited with him. Here there are four possibilities: because the destroyed thing is either deposited with the minor or not deposited, and this thing is either a slave or something else. The author did not mention the ruling for a non-deposited slave because it is obvious—it is guarantee. And the difference between a deposited slave and deposited property according to Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad. Abū Yūsuf and al-Shāfiʿī said: the minor guarantees in both cases. On this, if a restricted slave is entrusted with property and the minor consumes it, he is not held for guarantee immediately according to Abū Ḥanīfa, but is held after emancipation; according to Abū Yūsuf and al-Shāfiʿī, he is held immediately. On this difference is the issue of acknowledgment regarding the slave and minor, and likewise repetition in them. Then Muḥammad stipulated in al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr that the minor be sane. And in al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr, he placed the issue for a minor aged twelve years, and that... [1] If [the minor destroys] a slave, he guarantees [the blood money] by killing; if it is property other than that, he does not guarantee it according to Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad, but he does guarantee according to Abū Yūsuf and al-Shāfiʿī, because he destroyed inviolable property. We said: other than a slave is inviolable for the right of the master, and he forfeited it by placing it in the hand of the minor. As for the slave, his inviolability is for his own right because he is remaining on the original freedom in matters of blood. Evidence that a non-sane person guarantees by consensus; and because authorizing is not considered in him, but his action is considered. Thus in al-Takmila. [1] His statement: 'he guarantees by killing' i.e., blood money becomes due on the minor's 'āqila by consensus. Thus in al-Jalabī. [2] His statement: 'because he destroyed property' i.e., valuable, inviolable property belonging to the owner, so guarantee is obligatory upon him, as if the deposit were a slave, or the minor was authorized for trade or for preservation by the guardian, and likewise if he destroys something not in his hand, and it is not inviolable because the authority of consumption is established. [3] His statement: 'we said'; its clarification: the minor destroyed property that is not inviolable, so he is not held for its guarantee, as if he destroyed it with his permission and consent; this is because inviolability is established as a right for him, and he forfeited it by placing it in a non-protective hand, so it does not remain inviolable unless he appoints another in his place for preservation, and there is no appointment here because he has no authority over the minor to bind him, nor does the minor have authority over himself to be bound, unlike the authorized one because he has authority over himself like an adult. And unlike when the deposit is a slave, because his inviolability is for his own right, or he remains on the original freedom in matters of blood, so his inviolability is for his own right, not for the owner; because the owner's inviolability is considered only in what he has authority to consume, so that he can allow others to consume it by authorization; and the master does not have authority to consume his slave, so he cannot allow others to do so; thus his authorization is not considered, and the minor guarantees by his consumption, unlike other properties.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from a work on Hanafi fiqh, discussing the liability of a minor (ṣabī) who destroys property that was deposited with him. The passage distinguishes between two types of property: a slave (ʿabd) and other property (māl). According to Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad, if a minor destroys a deposited slave, his ʿāqila (agnatic group) is liable for blood money, but if he destroys other deposited property, he is not liable. Abū Yūsuf and al-Shāfiʿī hold that the minor is liable in both cases. The rationale is based on the concept of ʿiṣma (inviolability). For a slave, inviolability is inherent to the slave's own right (since a slave is considered free in matters of blood), so the depositor's act of entrusting the slave to a minor does not remove that inviolability. For other property, inviolability is a right of the owner, and by placing it in the hands of a minor (who is not legally capable of protecting it), the owner forfeits that inviolability, so the minor is not liable. The passage also analogizes to the case of a usurper (ghāṣib) who moves goods to a dangerous place, causing destruction, where liability attaches due to causation. The commentator explains that the ruling is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and contrasts with qiyās (analogy). The four scenarios are: (1) deposited slave destroyed → minor liable; (2) deposited property other than slave destroyed → minor not liable; (3) non-deposited slave destroyed → minor liable; (4) non-deposited property destroyed → minor liable (the last two are obvious). The discussion also touches on whether the minor is immediately held liable or after emancipation, with Abū Ḥanīfa preferring deferment and Abū Yūsuf/Shāfiʿī preferring immediate liability.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabī): A minor child who has not reached puberty. In this context, the ruling applies when the minor is not authorized by his guardian for transactions or preservation.
وديعة (wadīʿa): A deposit; property entrusted to someone for safekeeping without compensation. The depositary is a trustee (amīn) and is not liable for loss unless negligent or transgressive.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property. In this passage, it refers to financial liability or blood money (diyah).
عاقلة (ʿāqila): The agnatic group (male relatives) of the offender who are collectively responsible for paying blood money (diyah) in cases of accidental homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad, what is the ruling if a minor destroys a deposited slave?
A) He is not liable because the slave's inviolability is for the owner.
B) He is liable, and blood money is due on his ʿāqila.
C) He is liable immediately from his own property.
D) He is not liable because the owner forfeited inviolability.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a minor's liability for destroying deposited property turns on whether the inviolability (ʿiṣma) is a right of the owner (forfeitable) or of the property itself (not forfeitable).

Minor's Liability for Consuming a Deposit: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minor's immediate liability for consuming a deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, and Imam Abu Yusuf on a minor's immediate liability for consuming a deposit accepted without guardian permission, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A minor's consumption of a deposit triggers liability only if the deposit was validly accepted—but Abu Yusuf sees consumption itself as a tort.

This passage presents a disagreement within the Hanafi school on whether a minor (sabi) who consumes a deposit without guardian permission must immediately pay compensation. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that the minor is not liable because the deposit was not validly accepted, while Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the act of consumption itself creates liability. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of the interplay between legal capacity and tort liability in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and act
Recognize that the subject is a minor (sabi) and the act is consumption (istihlak) of a deposit (wadi'ah).
The minor may be interdicted (mahjur 'alayh) or permitted to trade.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario A: minor is permitted to trade or accepted deposit with guardian permission → liable by consensus. Scenario B: minor accepted deposit without permission → disputed.
The dispute only concerns Scenario B.
3
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad)
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the minor is not liable immediately nor after the deposit (i.e., not at all).
Their reasoning: the deposit was invalidly accepted, so no trust duty arises.
4
State the opposing position (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf holds the minor liable immediately.
His reasoning: consumption itself is a tort (itlaf) warranting liability.
5
Identify the consensus point
All agree that if the minor consumes property without a deposit, he is liable immediately.
This shows that the dispute is specific to the deposit context.
6
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the guardian does not have to pay compensation immediately; under Abu Yusuf, immediate payment is required.
The mufta bihi is not specified in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في «العناية»: وإذا استهلك الصبي ينظرُ إن كان مأذوناً له في التجارة، وإن كان محجوراً عليه، لكنه قبل الوديعة بإذن وليه، ضَمِنَ بالإجماع إن كان محجوراً عليه، وقبلها بغير أمر وليه، فلا ضمان عليه عند الإمام و محمد [الله؟] في الحال ولا بعد الإنزال. وقال أبو يوسف: يضمنُ في الحال، وأجمعوا على أنه لو استهلك مال الغير من غير أن يكون عنده وديعة، يضمنُ في الحال، وهو تقسيم حسن، هكذا في «التكملة».
He said in al-'Inayah: When a minor consumes (property), look: if he was permitted to trade, and if he was interdicted, but he accepted the deposit with his guardian's permission, he is liable by consensus if he was interdicted. If he accepted it without his guardian's order, then there is no liability upon him according to al-Imam and Muhammad, immediately nor after the deposit. Abu Yusuf said: He is liable immediately. And they all agreed that if he consumed someone else's property without having a deposit, he is liable immediately. This is a good division, thus in al-Takmilah.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a minor (sabi) who consumes (istahlaka) property that he received as a deposit (wadi'ah). The text distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If the minor is already permited to trade (ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijarah) or, though interdicted (mahjur 'alayh), he accepted the deposit with his guardian's permission, then he is liable by consensus. (2) If he accepted the deposit without his guardian's permission, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, he is not liable immediately (fi al-hal) nor after the deposit (ba'd al-inzal). However, Abu Yusuf holds that he is liable immediately. The passage notes that if the minor consumed property belonging to another without there being a deposit (i.e., through direct usurpation), all agree that he is liable immediately. The commentator considers this classification (taqsim) good. This dispute hinges on the capacity of the minor: when the guardian has not authorized acceptance, the deposit is not validly accepted, so no liability arises for loss until the property is actually consumed? The ruling from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad treats the unauthorized acceptance as void, thus no immediate liability; Abu Yusuf sees the consumption itself as a tort (itlaf) warranting immediate liability. The mufta bihi position is not specified here.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor who has not reached puberty; in this context, one who is interdicted (mahjur 'alayh) unless permitted by guardian.
الوديعة (al-wadi'ah): Deposit: property entrusted to another for safekeeping.
الاستهلاك (al-istihlak): Consumption: using up the deposited property, which constitutes transgression (ta'addi) making the depositary liable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when is a minor NOT liable for consuming a deposit?
A) When the minor is permitted to trade
B) When the minor accepted the deposit without guardian permission
C) When the minor consumed property that was not a deposit
D) When the minor consumed the deposit with guardian permission

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally disagrees on whether a minor's consumption of an invalidly accepted deposit triggers immediate liability, with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad denying it and Abu Yusuf affirming it.

Definition and Recommended Scope of Wills (Wasaya) in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines وصية and gives ruling categories with fiqh preferences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wasiyyah, classify the four rulings of wills, and apply the recommended scope of bequeathing less than one-third.

Core Idea
A will is a deferred transfer of ownership; bequeathing less than one-third is recommended even to wealthy heirs.

This passage from the Book of Wills opens with the legal definition of a will (wasiyyah) in Hanafi fiqh, then categorizes wills by ruling and elaborates on the recommended scope. Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines conditions like the need for acceptance. The author also explains the preference for bequeathing less than one-third or leaving entirely, citing the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Dissect the definition
Identify the three key elements in the definition: تمليك (transfer of ownership), مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت (deferred until after death), بطريق التبرع (voluntary act). These distinguish a will from a gift (effective immediately) and a sale (requires exchange).
The linguistic root same as وصية, but here it's a legal term.
2
Classify the four types of wills
List the four categories: obligatory (wajib, e.g., missed zakah), permissible (mubah, e.g., to a rich person), disliked (makruh, e.g., to immoral people), and recommended (mustahabb). Focus on the recommended type as the main subject.
The author starts with the fourth type to emphasize it.
3
Understand the recommended scope
Bequeathing less than one-third is always recommended even if heirs are wealthy. The proof: the Prophet said 'the one-third is much', implying that the full third is considerable, so less is better. Reducing the bequest is an act of connecting with relatives.
The hadith 'The best charity is upon the relative who harbors rancor' supports leaving the bequest entirely when heirs are poor.
4
Weigh between bequeathing and leaving entirely
When heirs are poor, leaving the will entirely is better because it is charity to a needy relative. When heirs are rich, bequeathing to a stranger is better because it is charity for Allah's sake. There is a choice when both options have merit.
This is a nuanced preference based on the status of the heirs.
5
Recognize the validity for a fetus
A will for a fetus is valid because it resembles inheritance (deputyship) where acceptance is not required. Although a will normally requires acceptance, its resemblance to inheritance overrides that condition for a fetus.
This shows the interplay of resemblance (shabah) in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا هي إيجاب بعد الموت، وندبت بأقل من الثلث عند غنى ورثته. ثم اعلم أن الوصايا جمع وصيّة، والوصية: اسم بمعنى المصدر، لما سمّي الموصى به وصية، وهي في الشرع تمليك مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت بطريق التبرع. الوصية أربعة أقسام: الأول واجبة: كالوصية بالزكاة وفدية الصلاة وفدية الصوم التي فرّط فيها. والثاني: مباحة كالوصية للغني. والثالث: مكروهة؛ كالوصية لأهل الفسوق. والرابع: مستحبة. وندبت الوصية بأقل من الثلث، ولو عند غنى ورثته. ويستحب أن يوصي بدون الثلث سواء كانت الورثة أغنياء أو فقراء؛ لأن في التنقيص صلة القريب بترك ماله عليهم، بخلاف استكماله الثلث؛ لأنه استيفاء تمام حقه، فلا صلة. ثم هل الوصية بأقل من الثلث أولى أم تركها؟ قالوا: إن كانت الورثة فقراء ولا يستغنون بما يرثون، فالترك أولى لما فيه من الصدقة على القريب، وقد قال: «أفضل الصدقة على ذي الرحم الكاشح». أو استغنائهم بحصتهم كتركها بلا أحدهما: أي إن لم تكن الورثة أغنياء ولا يصيرون أغنياء بحصتهم من التّركة، فترك الوصية أفضل. وصحت للحمل وإن كانوا أغنياء أو يستغنون بنصيبهم فالوصيّة أولى؛ لأنه يكون صدقة على الأجنبي، والترك هبة من القريب، والأولى أولى؛ لأنه من يبتغي بها وجه الله تعالى، وقيل في هذا الوجه يخير لاشتمال كل على فضيلة، وهو الصدقة أو الصلة. وحاصله أنه لا ينبغي الوصية بتمام الثلث، بل المستحب التنقيص عنه مطلقاً؛ لأنه قد استكثر الثلث بقوله: «والثلث كثير»، لكن التنقيص عنه فقر الورثة، وإن كان مستحباً إلا أن ثمة ما هو أولى منه، وهو الترك أصلاً؛ فإن المستحب تتفاوت درجاته، وكذا المسنون والمكروه وغيرهما. وفي القهستاني: إذا كان المال قليلاً لا ينبغي أن يوصي على ما قال أبو حنيفة، وهذا إذا كان الأولاد كباراً، فلو صغاراً فالترك أفضل مطلقاً على ما روي عن الشيخين. وصحت للحمل؛ لأنها استخلاف من وجه؛ لأنه يجعله خليفة في بعض ماله، والجنين يصلح خليفة في الإرث؛ فكذا في الوصية. لا يقال: شرطها القبول، والجنين ليس من أهله؛ لأنها تشبه الهبة والميراث، فلشبهها بالهبة يشترط القبول إذا كان الموصى له أهلاً للقبول، والجنين ليس أهلاً للقبول؛ لكن لما شابهت الميراث لا يشترط القبول، فتصح للجنين.
Book of Wills: It is an obligation after death, and it is recommended with less than one-third when the heirs are wealthy. Know that وصايا is the plural of وصية, and وصية is a noun in the sense of the verbal noun, because the bequeathed property is called وصية. In law it is a transfer of ownership added to after death by way of donation. Wills are of four types: First, obligatory: like a will for zakah and the redemption of prayer and fasting which were neglected. Second, permissible: like a will for a rich person. Third, disliked: like a will for immoral people. Fourth, recommended. The author began with the fourth type by saying: and it is recommended. The will is recommended with less than one-third, even if the heirs are wealthy. It is recommended to bequeath less than one-third whether the heirs are rich or poor, because reducing creates connection with the relative by leaving wealth to them, unlike completing the third, for that is taking one's full right, so there is no connection. Then is it better to bequeath less than one-third or to leave it? They said: If the heirs are poor and do not become independent by what they inherit, then leaving is better because it is charity for the relative, and he said: 'The best charity is upon the relative who harbors rancor.' Or if they become independent by their share, like leaving it, without either one: meaning if the heirs are not rich and do not become rich by their share of the estate, then leaving the will is better. And it is valid for the fetus. And if they are rich or become rich by their share, then the will is better, because it is charity to a stranger, and leaving is a gift to a relative, and the better is better because one seeks thereby the face of Allah. It is said in this case he is given choice because each includes a virtue: charity or connection. The summary: One should not bequeath the full third; rather it is recommended to reduce from it absolutely, because he considered the third much by his saying: 'And the third is much.' However, reducing from it [when] the heirs are poor, although it is recommended, there is something better than it, which is leaving entirely; for recommended acts have varying degrees, and likewise al-sunnah and al-makruh and others. In al-Qahistani: If the wealth is little, one should not bequeath according to Abu Hanifah; this is if the children are adult, but if young, then leaving is absolutely better as narrated from the two shaykhs. And it is valid for the fetus, because it is a kind of deputyship; since he makes him a deputy over some of his wealth, and the fetus is suitable as a deputy in inheritance, so likewise in the will. It cannot be said: Its condition is acceptance, and the fetus is not capable of it; because it resembles a gift and inheritance. Due to its resemblance to a gift, acceptance is required if the legatee is capable of acceptance, and the fetus is not capable; but because it resembles inheritance, acceptance is not required, so it is valid for the fetus.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Wills (كتاب الوصايا) gives the definition and legal classification of a will in Hanafi fiqh. The author first defines وصية linguistically and legally. Legally, it is a transfer of ownership (تمليك) postponed until after death, done voluntarily (تبرع). He then classifies wills into four categories based on the ruling: obligatory (واجبة) for neglected religious duties, permissible (مباحة) for a wealthy person, disliked (مكروهة) for immoral people, and recommended (مستحبة) which is the focus here. The recommended will is one that bequeaths less than one-third of the estate, even if the heirs are wealthy, because reducing one's bequest to less than the maximum allowed (one third) is a way to show generosity to relatives by leaving more for them. The author cites the famous hadith 'The best charity is on the relative who harbors rancor' to support leaving the bequest when heirs are poor. However, if the heirs are already wealthy or become wealthy through their share, then bequeathing to a non-relative (charity to a stranger) is better than giving to relatives (who are already independent). The passage ends by discussing the validity of a will for a fetus (حمل): it is valid because it resembles an appointment of a deputy in inheritance, and the fetus can inherit, so it can be a legatee. Although a will normally requires acceptance, since a will also resembles a gift, acceptance from a capable person is needed; but because it also resembles inheritance, acceptance is not required from the fetus, making the will valid. The author notes that the obligatory will is for missed worship like zakah, fasting, and prayer, which must be fulfilled from the estate.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A legal testament: a transfer of ownership deferred until after death, done voluntarily.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; giving possession to another.
تبرع (tabarru'): Voluntary donation without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on bequeathing less than one-third of one's estate when the heirs are wealthy?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is prohibited (haram).
C) It is recommended (mustahabb).
D) It is permissible but not recommended.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines a will as a deferred voluntary transfer of ownership and strongly recommends bequeathing less than one-third, with preference for leaving entirely when heirs need support.

Bequests of Slaves: Proportional Reduction from One-Third
Explains rulings for bequests exceeding one-third with two slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the amounts received by multiple legatees when total bequests exceed one-third, applying proportional reduction under the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Bequests exceeding one-third are not void; they are proportionally reduced to fit within the one-third limit.

This lesson examines two related scenarios from the chapter of bequests (wasaya) where a testator leaves instructions involving two slaves, but the total bequests exceed the one-third limit. The Hanafi ruling is that such bequests remain valid but are enforced only up to one-third of the estate, with any surplus among multiple legatees distributed proportionally. We will work through the calculations step by step, including the unique 'sa'yah' (work) requirement for partially freed slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the total estate value
Sum the values of all assets left by the testator. In the purchase case, two slaves worth 30 and 60 give a total estate of 90.
2
Determine the one-third limit
Multiply the total estate by 1/3. For an estate of 90, the one-third limit is 30.
3
Identify each bequest's amount
In the purchase case, the bequest is the difference between the slave's value and the sale price: for Zaid, 30-10=20; for Amr, 60-20=40. In the saya case, the bequests are shares: 1/3 of the estate for the first slave and 2/3 for the second.
4
Calculate the ratio of bequests
Divide each bequest by the total bequests. For purchase: total bequests = 20+40=60, ratio Zaid:20/60=1/3, Amr:40/60=2/3. For saya: bequest shares are 1/3 and 2/3 of the property, ratio 1:2.
5
Distribute the one-third proportionally
Multiply the one-third limit by each legatee's ratio. For purchase: Zaid gets 30 * (1/3) = 10, Amr gets 30 * (2/3) = 20. For saya: first slave gets 30 * (1/3) = 10 freed, second gets 30 * (2/3) = 20 freed. The remaining values (20 and 40) must be earned through sa'yah.
Sa'yah is the work the partially freed slave performs to pay for the remainder of their value.

Source Text

عبدان قيمة أحدهما ثلاثون، والآخر ستون، فأوصى بأن يباع الأول من زيد بعشرة، والآخر من عمرو بعشرين، ولا مال له سواهما، فالوصية في حق زيد بعشرين، وفي حق عمرو بأربعين، يقسم الثلث بينهما أثلاثاً فيباع الأول من زيد بعشرين، والعشرة وصية له، ويباع الثاني من عمرو بأربعين، والعشرون وصية له، فأخذ عمرو من الثلث بقدر وصيته، وإن كانت زائدة على الثلث. وصورة السعاية: أعتق عبدين قيمتهما ما ذكر، ولا مال له سواهما، فالوصية للأول بثلث المال والثاني بثلثي المال، فسهام الوصية بينهما أثلاث، واحد للأول، واثنان للثاني، فيقسم الثلث بينهما كذلك، فيعتق من الأول ثلاثة، وهو عشرة، ويسعى في عشرين، ويعتق من الثاني ثلثه، وهو عشرون، ويسعى في أربعين، فيضرب كل بقدر وصيته وإن كان زائداً على الثلث.
[1] قوله : فأخذ . الثلث بقدر وصيته ؛ لأنَّ وصيَّته له أربعون من ستين ، وهو ثلثاه ، وقدرها من ثلث جميع المال الذي هو ثلاثون، ثلثاه منه، وهو عشرون. فلو كان هذا كسائر الوصايا وجب على قول أبي حنيفة له أن لا يضرب الموصى له بأربعين في أكثر من ثلثين ؛ لأنَّ عنده الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث لا يضرب إلا بالثلث وهو ثلث ماله. هذا حاصل ما في شرح الأكمل». كذا في «الجلبي))) ٢ ] قوله : وإن كانت ؛ أي وصية لعمرو، وهي أربعون زائدة على الثلث : أي على ثلث الكلِّ الذي هو تسعون هو الثلاثون كذا في الجلبي» [٣] قوله : أعتق عبدين ؛ أي أوصى مريض بعتق عبديه ؛ قيمة أحدهما ستون والآخر ثلاثون . [٤] قوله : فيضرب كلّ ؛ أي يأخذ ولو كانت وصيّة فيما عدا السعاية ؛ لكان الثلث الذي هـو الثلاثون نصفين بين العبدين عند أبي.
Two slaves, the value of one being thirty and the other sixty, and he bequeathed that the first be sold to Zaid for ten, and the other to Amr for twenty, and he has no other property besides these two. So the bequest in favor of Zaid is twenty, and in favor of Amr is forty. The one-third is divided between them into thirds. So the first is sold to Zaid for twenty, and ten is his bequest, and the second is sold to Amr for forty, and twenty is his bequest. So Amr takes from the one-third according to the amount of his bequest, even if it exceeds the one-third. And the form of sa'yah: He freed two slaves whose values were as mentioned, and he has no other property besides them. So the bequest for the first is one-third of the property, and for the second is two-thirds of the property. The shares of the bequest between them are thirds: one for the first, two for the second. So the one-third is divided between them likewise. So one-third of the first is freed, which is ten, and he works for twenty, and one-third of the second is freed, which is twenty, and he works for forty. So each takes according to his bequest even if it exceeds the one-third.
[1] His statement: 'So Amr took from the one-third according to his bequest' because his bequest for him is forty out of sixty, which is two-thirds of it, and its amount from the one-third of the total property, which is thirty, is two-thirds of it, which is twenty. So if this were like other bequests, it would be necessary according to Abu Hanifa that the legatee of forty does not take more than two-thirds, because according to him, the legatee of more than one-third only takes one-third, which is one-third of his property. This is the summary from Sharh al-Akmal. As in al-Jalabi. [2] His statement: 'even if it exceeds' i.e., the bequest to Amr, which is forty, exceeds the one-third, i.e., the one-third of the whole which is ninety is thirty. As in al-Jalabi. [3] His statement: 'He freed two slaves' i.e., a sick person bequeathed the freeing of his two slaves; the value of one is sixty and the other thirty. [4] His statement: 'So each takes' i.e., he takes. If it were a bequest other than sa'yah, the one-third, which is thirty, would be divided into halves between the two slaves according to Abu.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings within the chapter of bequests (wasaya). The first ruling concerns a bequest to sell slaves at a price below their value, where the difference is treated as a bequest. The second ruling concerns the 'saya' case, where a sick person bequeaths the freeing of slaves, and the bequest exceeds one-third. The key principle is that when the total bequests exceed one-third of the estate, the bequests are proportionally reduced to fit within the one-third. In the first example, two slaves are valued at 30 and 60 dirhams respectively. The testator bequeaths that the first slave be sold to Zaid for 10 and the second to Amr for 20. Since the actual values are higher, the bequest amounts are the differences: 20 for Zaid (30-10) and 40 for Amr (60-20). The total bequests are 60, but the one-third of the estate (total value 90) is 30. So the 30 is divided proportionally between Zaid and Amr in the ratio 20:40, i.e., 1:2. Thus Zaid gets 10 and Amr gets 20 from the one-third. Although Amr's bequest was 40, he only receives 20 from the one-third, and the sale goes through at the specified prices. The commentary notes that according to Abu Hanifa, a legatee whose bequest exceeds one-third does not take more than one-third. In the saya case, the testator frees two slaves worth 30 and 60. He bequeaths one-third of his property to the first and two-thirds to the second. The total bequests are one-third and two-thirds, which together equal the whole property, but the one-third of the estate is only 30. So the one-third is divided in the ratio of the bequest shares: 1:2. Thus, from the one-third, the first slave gets 10 (one-third of 30) and the second gets 20 (two-thirds of 30). The remaining value of each slave (20 from the first and 40 from the second) must be earned through work (saya) to complete their freedom. This shows that even when the bequest explicitly exceeds one-third, it is not void; rather, it is honored within the one-third limit.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by a person regarding their property after death.
سعاية (sa'yah): The work a partially freed slave must perform to earn the remaining portion of their value.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum amount that can be bequeathed without heirs' permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the 'saya' case with two slaves valued at 30 and 60, what are the respective amounts the slaves must earn through work?
A) 10 and 20
B) 20 and 40
C) 30 and 60
D) 15 and 30

Key Takeaway
Bequests exceeding one-third are valid but proportionally reduced; in manumission by bequest, the shortfall is earned through sa'yah.

Unrestricted Dirham Bequests and Bequests Like a Son's Share
Distinguishes between quantified bequests and unrestricted amounts with ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid bequest expressions in Hanafi law and apply the proportional reduction rule for unrestricted dirham bequests.

Core Idea
Unrestricted dirham bequests reduce proportionally; 'like the son's share' is valid, 'the son's share' is not.

This passage clarifies two subtle rulings in bequests: (1) when a testator bequeaths specific sums that exceed one-third, the bequest is not void but proportionally reduced, and (2) the crucial difference between bequeathing 'like' a son's share versus 'the' son's share. Understanding these distinctions prevents common errors in estate planning and ensures the testator's intentions are honoured within legal limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of bequests discussed
The passage covers unrestricted dirham bequests (specific amounts) and bequests phrased as 'like the share of my son' versus 'the share of my son'. Locate each in the text.
2
Apply the proportional reduction rule for unrestricted dirhams
When total bequests exceed one-third of the estate, the one-third is divided proportionally among the legatees according to the amounts bequeathed, not equally.
This differs from fractional bequests where the excess is void outright.
3
Compare 'like the share' and 'the share'
Abu Hanifa holds that 'like the share' is valid because it refers to something separate, while 'the share' is invalid because it bequeaths property that belongs to the son as heir.
Zufar dissents, considering the actual outcome rather than the wording.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Zufar's view that 'the share' is valid is a legitimate opinion but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's, making such bequests invalid.
This dispute affects whether the legatee receives anything.

وصورة الدراهم المرسلة : أوصى لزيد بثلاثين درهما، وللآخر بستين درهما وماله تسعون درهما، فيضرب كل بقدر وصيته " ، فيضربُ الأَوَّلُ الثُّلُثَ فِي ثُلُثِ المال، والثاني الثلثين في ثلث المال. والمراد بالمرسلة المطلقة : أي غير مقيدة بأنها ثلث، أو نصف، أو نحوهما. وإنما فَرَّقَ أبو حنيفة بين هذه الصور الثلاث وبين غيرها ؛ لأنَّ الوصية إذا كانت مقدرة بما زاد على الثلث صريحاً كالنصف ، والثلثين، وغيرهما، والشَّرْعُ أبطل الوصية في الزائد، يكون ذِكْرُهُ لغواً ، فلا يعتبر في حق الضَّرِب بخلاف ما إذا لم تكن مقدرة بأنها أي شيءٍ من المال كما في الصور الثَّلاثِ ، فإِنَّه ليس في العبارة ما يكون مبطلاً للوصية، كما إذا أوصى بخمسين درهماً، واتفق أن ماله مئة درهم، فإنَّ الوصية غير باطلة بالكلية ؛ لإمكان أن يَظْهَرَ له مالٌ فوق المئة ، وإذا لم تكن باطلة بالكلّيّة، يكونُ معتبرة في حقٌّ الضَّرَّب، وهذا فرق دقيق شريف. And the form of unrestricted dirhams: He bequeathed to Zaid thirty dirhams, and to the other sixty dirhams, and his property is ninety dirhams. So each takes according to his bequest: the first takes one-third of one-third of the property, and the second takes two-thirds of one-third of the property. By 'unrestricted' is meant absolute, i.e., not restricted as being one-third, half, or the like. Abu Hanifa distinguished between these three forms and others because when the bequest is explicitly quantified as exceeding the one-third, like half, two-thirds, etc., and the law invalidates the bequest in the excess, its mention becomes superfluous, so it is not considered with regard to taking. Unlike when it is not quantified as any portion of the property, as in these three forms, for there is nothing in the expression that invalidates the bequest, just as if he bequeaths fifty dirhams and it happens that his property is one hundred dirhams, then the bequest is not entirely invalid because it is possible that he may have property above one hundred. And when it is not entirely invalid, it is considered with regard to taking. This is a subtle and noble distinction. (And with 'like the share of his son') it is valid, (and with 'the share of his son') it is not, because the bequest of what is the son's right is not valid for another. There is a difference of opinion with Zufar on this.
[1] His statement: 'So each takes according to his bequest...' If the unrestricted bequest were like other bequests, the one-third of the dirhams would be divided between them in halves. As in al-Jalabi. [2] His statement: 'And with like the share of his son...' Explanation: If he bequeaths 'like the share of his son,' the bequest is valid; if he bequeaths 'the share of his son,' it is not valid. Because in the first form, it is a bequest of something like the son's share, and 'like' a thing is other than it, even if it is estimated, so it is permissible. In the second, it is a bequest of what is the son's right, which is what the son receives after death, and what he receives is the property of another, so bequest of property is not valid. Zufar said: It is valid in this case too, as in the first, considering the situation, not the completion.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage defines and rules on two distinct issues within bequests. First, the 'unrestricted dirhams' (الدراهم المرسلة) case: when a testator bequeaths specific amounts of money (e.g., 30 and 60 dirhams) and the total exceeds one-third of the estate. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between bequests that are explicitly quantified as fractions of the estate (like half, two-thirds) and those that are stated as absolute amounts. In the latter, the bequest is not automatically void because there is a possibility that the testator may have additional property beyond what is known, so the bequest is considered valid up to one-third. Therefore, the one-third is divided proportionally according to the bequest amounts: if the bequests are 30 and 60, the ratio is 1:2, so from the one-third, the first gets 10 and the second gets 20. Second, the issue of bequests 'like the share of his son' versus 'the share of his son'. If the testator says 'I bequeath like the share of my son,' it is valid because 'like' indicates something similar to but not identical to the son's share. However, if he says 'I bequeath the share of my son,' it is invalid because that share belongs to the son as an heir, and one cannot bequeath what is another's property. Zufar disagrees and holds that even the second is valid, looking at the actual outcome rather than the wording.

Key Terms
الدراهم المرسلة (ad-darahim al-mursalah): Bequests of specific amounts of dirhams without reference to fractions of the estate.
مثل نصيب ابنه (mithlu naseebi ibnihi): A bequest of a share 'like' the son's share, considered a valid bequest of something similar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa consider a bequest of 'the share of my son' invalid?
A) Because it may exceed one-third
B) Because it is a bequest of another's property (the son's right as heir)
C) Because the son must consent
D) Because it is not specified as a fraction

Key Takeaway
The precise wording of a bequest determines its validity: unrestricted amounts are proportionally reduced, 'like the share' is valid, but 'the share' is invalid.

Bequest of a Part and a Share: Hanafi Rulings and Intra-School Dispute
Commentary on bequest rulings with proof and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a bequest of an unspecified part (juz') and a share (sahm), and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the interpretation of 'sahm'.

Core Idea
A bequest of a 'share' means one-sixth in Kufan custom, per Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn say it means the smallest heir's share.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah deals with two common types of ambiguous bequests: a 'part' (juz') and a 'share' (sahm). While bequest of a part is left to the heirs to specify, bequest of a share has a fixed meaning according to custom. However, the Hanafi school is divided on what that fixed meaning is. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses bequests of two ambiguous terms: 'juz'' (part) and 'sahm' (share). For 'juz'', the ruling is that the bequest is valid and the heirs determine the amount. For 'sahm', there is a dispute within the Hanafi school.
2
State the Hanafi position on 'juz''
Bequest of a part is valid despite uncertainty; the heirs specify the quantum because they stand in the testator's place. Ignorance does not invalidate the bequest due to the lenient scope of bequest law.
3
State the Hanafi position on 'sahm' according to Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa holds that 'sahm' in Kufan custom means one-sixth (sudus). This is supported by a marfu' hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and the linguistic definition by Iyas.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut, but accepted as a proof for custom.
4
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that 'sahm' means one of the heirs' shares, so the legatee gets the smallest heir's share, not exceeding one-third unless the heirs authorize more. Their proof is the customary usage in bequests.
The Sahibayn prioritize general custom over the specific Kufan custom and hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view (one-sixth). The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the legatee always gets one-sixth; under the Sahibayn, he gets the smallest heir's share (which could be less) but capped at one-third.
Tarjih by al-Hidayah and followed in this commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا / تعريفها وأحكامها
وله ثلث إن أوصى مع ابنين وبجزء من مالِهِ يُبيِّنُهُ الورثة، وبسهم السدس في عرفهم، وهو كالجزء في عُرفنا

[١] قوله : وله ثلث... الخ ؛ أي إن أوصى مع ابنين بمثل نصيب ابنه، فللموصى له الثلث، والقياس أن يكونَ النصفُ عند إجازة الورثة ؛ لأنه أوصى له بمثل نصيب ابنه ، ونصيب كلِّ واحدٍ منهما النصف. ووجه الثلث أنّ قصده أن يجعله مثل ابنه ونصيبه مثل نصيب ابنه، لا أن يجعل نصيبه زائداً على نصيب ابنه، وذلك بأن يجعل الموصى لــه كأحدهم. كذا في «الزيلعي»

[٢] قوله : ويجزء... الخ ؛ أي ولو أوصى بجزء من ماله ، يقال للورثة : أعطوه ما شئتم ؛ لأنّ الجزء مجهول، يتناولُ القليل والكثير غير أن الجهالة لا تمنع صحة الوصية ؛ لأن باب الوصيّة أوسع، والورثة قائمون مقام الموصي ، فإليهم البيان، هذا توضيح ما في الشرح.

[٣] قوله : وبسهم ... الخ ؛ أي إن أوصى بسهم من ماله ، فله السدس في عرفهم ؛ أي عرف أهل الكوفة، وهو أي السدس كالجزء في عرفنا : أي الوصية بسهم من ماله كالوصية بجزء من ماله. (۱) (الهداية» (٤ : ٢٣٧). (۲) تبيين الحقائق» (۱ : ۱۸۸ - ۱۸۹).

فإن قال : سدس مالي له ، ثُمَّ قال : ثلثه له ، وأجازوا، له ثلث فإن قال : سدس مالي له ، ثم قال : ثلثه له ، وأجازوا ، له ثلث : أي يكون السُّدُسُ داخلاً في الثلث، فإن قلت : قولُهُ: ثُلُثُ مالي له ؛ إن كان إخباراً فكاذب، وان كان إنشاء يجب أن يكون له النِّصْفُ عند إجازة الورثة ، وإن كان في السدس إخبار وفي السدس إنشاء ، فهذا ممتنع أيضاً.

قال في «الهداية»: ومن أوصى بسهم من ماله فله أحسن سهام الورثة إلا أن ينقص عن السدس ، فيتم له السدس، ولا يزاد عليه مآل المصنف به وصاحب «الهداية» واحد، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له.
وقالا : له مثل نصيب أحد الورثة الذي له أقلّ الأنصباء، ولا يزاد على الثلث إلا أن تجيز الورثة ؛ لأنّ السهم يراد به أحد سهام الورثة عرفاً، لا سيما في الوصية، والأقل متيقن به فيصرفُ إليه إلا إذا زاد على الثلث فيرد عليه ؛ لأنه لا مزيد عليه عند عدم الإجارة.
وله : إن السهم هو السدس، هو المروي عن ابن مسعود ، وقد رفعه إلى النبي ﷺ فيما يروى ؛ ولأنه يذكر ويراد به السدس ، فإن إياسا له قال : السهم في اللغة عبارة عن السدس، ويذكر ويراد به سهم من سهام الورثة فيعطى ما ذكرنا انتهى

[١] قوله : له ثلث ; قال صاحب (رد المحتار) : «أقول : حاصل السؤال أنّ قولَ الموصي : ثلث مالي له لا يصلح إخباراً ؛ لأنه كذب، فتعين الإنشاء، فينبغي أن يكون له النصف ؛ لأنّ عموم السدس والثلث النصف والربع أنا سلّمنا أن قوله : سدس مالي له يحتمل أن يكون المراد به زيادة سدس أو ثلثاً آخر غير السدس المذكور، فيحمل على المتيقن.
وبقي هاهنا شيء، وهو أنه لا يخلو من أن يكون الثلث الذي أجازه الورثة ثلثاً زائداً على السدس الذي أجازوه ؛ أو لا يكون ثلثاً زائداً عليه، أو لا وجه لإجازتهم بلا تعيين المراد، إذ مرجعه إلى إجازة اللفظ ، ولا معنى له والثاني يأباه قوله : وأجازوا ؛ لأنه مستغن عن إجازتهم، وعلى الأول لا يصح الجواب المذكور.
Book of Bequests / Its definition and rulings. He gets one third if he bequeaths with two sons and with a part of his wealth which the heirs specify, and with a share of one sixth in their custom, and it is like a part in our custom. [1] His statement: 'And he gets one third... etc.' means: If he bequeaths with two sons something like the share of his son, then the legatee gets one third. By analogy it would be half upon the permission of the heirs, because he bequeathed to him something like the share of his son, and the share of each of them is half. The [reason for] one third is that his intent is to make him like his son and his share like his son's share, not to make his share exceed his son's share. That is by making the legatee like one of them. As in al-Zaylai. [2] His statement: 'And with a part... etc.' means: If he bequeaths a part of his wealth, the heirs are told: Give him whatever you wish, because the part is unknown, including little and much; but ignorance does not prevent the validity of the bequest, because the scope of bequest is wider, and the heirs stand in place of the testator, so clarification is up to them. This explains what is in the Sharh. [3] His statement: 'And with a share... etc.' means: If he bequeaths a share of his wealth, he gets one sixth in their custom, i.e. the custom of the people of Kufa. And it, i.e. the sixth, is like a part in our custom: i.e. a bequest of a share of his wealth is like a bequest of a part of his wealth. (1) Al-Hidayah (4:237). (2) Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (1:188-189). If he says: One sixth of my wealth belongs to him, then says: One third of it belongs to him, and they authorize it, he gets one third. If he says: One sixth of my wealth, then says: One third of it, and they authorize it, he gets one third, meaning the sixth is included in the third. If you say: His statement 'One third of my wealth belongs to him' — if it is a report, it is false; if it is a declaration, it should be that he gets half upon the heirs' permission; and if the sixth is a report and the sixth [sic] is a declaration, this is also impossible. He said in al-Hidayah: Whoever bequeaths a share of his wealth gets the best of the heirs' shares, unless it falls short of one sixth, then he completes it to one sixth, and it is not increased beyond it. The conclusion of the author and the author of al-Hidayah is one, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. The two said: He gets like the share of one of the heirs who has the smallest share, and it is not increased to more than one third unless the heirs authorize it, because 'share' is customarily used for one of the shares of the heirs, especially in bequests, and the least is certain so it is applied to it, unless it exceeds one third then it is reduced, because there is no increase upon it in the absence of authorization. And there is [proof] that the share is one sixth, as narrated from Ibn Mas'ud, and he raised it to the Prophet ﷺ in what is narrated; and because it is mentioned and intended to mean one sixth, for Iyas said: 'Share' in language means one sixth, and it is mentioned and intended to mean a share from the shares of the heirs, so he is given what we mentioned. End. [1] His statement: 'He gets one third'; the author of Radd al-Muhtar said: I say: The gist of the question is that the testator's statement 'One third of my wealth belongs to him' is not valid as a report because it is false, so it is determined as a declaration, so it should be that he gets half, because the inclusive [meaning] of sixth and third is half and quarter. But we concede that his statement 'One sixth of my wealth belongs to him' may mean an additional sixth or another third besides the mentioned sixth, so it is interpreted according to the certain [meaning]. And there remains something here: it is that it is either that the third which the heirs authorized is a third in addition to the sixth which they authorized, or it is not an additional third; there is no basis for their authorization without specifying the intended meaning, since it reduces to authorization of the wording, which is meaningless; the second is rejected by his statement 'and they authorized' because it is independent of their authorization; and on the first, the mentioned answer is not correct.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the Sharh al-Wiqayah, discussing the rulings of bequests involving 'part' (juz') and 'share' (sahm). The author first clarifies the matn: if a testator leaves two sons and bequeaths 'misl naseeb ibnihi' (like the share of his son), the legatee gets one-third, not half, because the testator's intent is to make the legatee like one of the sons, so the bequest is divided as if there were three sons (the two real sons plus the legatee), giving each one-third. This is contrary to qiyas (analogy) which would give half if the heirs authorize, but the ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) considering the testator's intent. Next, if the bequest is 'a part of my wealth' (juz' min mali), the part is unknown, but the bequest is valid; the heirs decide what to give because they stand in the testator's place. Ignorance does not invalidate because the law of bequest is lenient. Then, if the bequest is 'a share of my wealth' (sahm min mali), according to Abu Hanifa the legatee gets one-sixth based on the Kufan custom where 'sahm' is understood as one-sixth. This is supported by a marfu' hadith narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that 'sahm' in language means one-sixth. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that 'sahm' means one of the heirs' shares, so the legatee gets the smallest heir's share, not exceeding one-third unless the heirs consent to more. They argue that custom particularly in bequests uses 'sahm' for heirs' shares, and the smaller amount is certain. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The commentator then addresses a scenario: if the testator first says 'one-sixth to him' then 'one-third to him' and the heirs authorize, the legatee gets one-third, as the third includes the sixth. A question arises about the nature of the second statement (whether it is a report or a declaration), and the author of Radd al-Muhtar resolves it by considering the intent to add an additional third. The passage ends with a discussion of authorization and the need to specify the meaning. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, as stated in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): An undefined part of the testator's wealth; the heirs specify the amount.
سهم (sahm): A share of the testator's wealth; in Kufan custom it means one-sixth, but generally it could mean any heir's share.
سدس (sudus): One-sixth; the quantum given to the legatee under Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a testator bequeaths 'a share of my wealth' (sahm min mali), what does the legatee receive?
A) The best of the heirs' shares
B) One-sixth of the estate
C) The smallest heir's share
D) One-third of the estate

Key Takeaway
A bequest of a 'share' (sahm) is interpreted as one-sixth in the relied-upon Hanafi view, based on custom and prophetic narration.

Acknowledging Debts Up to One-Third with Bequests
Hanafi ruling on debt acknowledgement up to one-third with bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on acknowledging an uncertain debt up to one-third of the estate and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A debt acknowledged by the testator is treated as a bequest, limiting the heirs' liability to one-third.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a testator's acknowledgement of a debt where the amount is uncertain. The heirs are commanded to believe the creditor up to one-third of the estate, based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than strict qiyas. The passage also explains how this interacts when the testator makes explicit bequests, requiring proportional contributions from the bequest and inheritance shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Locate the sentence 'وفي له علي دين فصدِّقُوه صُدِّقَ إلى الثلث' and understand that the heirs must acknowledge the debt up to one-third. Note that this is established by istihsan, not qiyas.
The ruling applies when the testator commands the heirs to believe the creditor.
2
Contrast with qiyas
Understand the qiyas position: normally a claimant is not believed without proof, so the acknowledgement would not be enforced. This sets up the need for istihsan.
Qiyas would render the command invalid, but istihsan gives effect to the testator's intention.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The testator's intention is to prioritize the creditor over heirs. This can be realized by treating the claim as a bequest, which is limited to one-third. Thus the heirs only bear the burden up to that limit.
The creditor's claim is treated as a bequest, so the one-third rule applies.
4
Apply the scenario with additional bequests
If the testator also makes explicit bequests, one-third is set aside for them, and two-thirds for heirs. Both groups must acknowledge the debt proportionally. The creditor takes from each group's share according to what they acknowledge.
This prevents the debt from automatically taking precedence over known bequests; it is settled proportionally.

Source Text

وفي له علي دين فصدِّقُوه صُدِّقَ إلى الثلث
نصيب زيد وعمرو متساويان، وقد أُشْرَكَ آخر معهما ، فهو شريك للاثنين، فله ثلث ما لكل واحد منهما ، ولا يمكن مثل هذا في الصورة الثانية ؛ لتفاوتِ نصيب زيد وعمرو ، فهو شريك لكل واحد ، فله نصف لكل واحد منهما. (وفي له علي دين فصدِّقُوه صُدِّقَ إلى الثلث) : أي أمر أن يُصدِّقوا الدائن في مقدار الدين ، يجب عليهم أن يصدقوه إلى الثلث ، فأصل الحقِّ دين ، ومقداره يثبت بطريق الوصية، وهذا استحسان، وفي القياس لا يُصَدَّق ؛ لأنَّ المدعي لا يُصَدِّقُ إلا بحجة.
[1]
ل : فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلث ) ، فيستوي الذكور والإناث في الثلث.
ففي الصورة الأولى نصيب زيد وعمرو متساويان وقد، أشرك آخر منهما فهو شريك للإثنين ، فله ثلث ما لكلِّ واحدٍ منهما ؛ لاتحاد المال، فللآخر يكون ثلاثمئة ، وهي ست وستون وثلثا درهم، كما لكل من زيد وعمرو.
بخلاف الصورة الثانية ؛ لأنه لا يمكن مثل هذا التفاوت نصیب زيد وعمرو، فله نصف ما لكل واحد منهما، وهو خمس وسبعون ؛ لأنه كان لزيد مئة ونصفها خمسون، ولعمرو خمسون، ونصفها لا خمسة وعشرون ولزيد ولعمرو خمسة وعشرون درهما. [١] قوله : لا يصدق ؛ لأنّ المقرَّ بالمجهول وإن كان صحيحاً لكنه لا يحكم به إلا بالبيان، وقوله: فصدقوة ؛ صدرَ مخالفاً للشرع ؛ لأن المدعي لا يصدق إلا بحجة فالأمر بتصديق المدعي من غير حجّة مخالف للشرع، فتعذر إثبات هذا الإقرار إقراراً مطلقاً، فلا يعتبر.
ووجه الاستحسان : أنا نعلمُ أنّ من قصدِهِ تقديمه على الورثة، وقد أمكن تنفيذ قصده بطريق الوصية، وقد يحتاجُ إليه من يعلمُ بأصل الحق عليه دون مقداره سعياً منه في تفريغ ذمته، فبجعلها وصيّة جعل التقدير فيها إلى الموصي له ، كأنه قال: إذا جاءكم
(۱) النساء : ١٢ .
فإن أوصى مع ذلك عُزل ثلث لها ، وثلثاه للورثة ، وقيل لكل : صدقوه فيما شئتم ، ويؤخذ ذو الثلث بثلث ما أقروا به، وما بقي فلهم، والورثة بثلثي ما أقروا به ، ويَحْلِفُ كل على العلم بدعوى الزيادة (فإن أوصى مع ذلك عُزل ثلث لها ، وثلثاه للورثة ، وقيل لكل : صدقوه فيما شئتم ، ويؤخذ ذو الثَّلُثِ بَثْلُثِ ما أقروا به ، وما بقي فلهم"، والورثة بثلثي ما أقروا به ، ويَحْلِفُ كلِّ على العلم بدعوى الزيادة) : أي أوصى مع ذلك الدين الذي أمر بتصديق مقدارِهِ بثُلُثِ مالهِ لقوم ، يُعْزَلُ ثُلُثُ المال للوصية والثلثان للورثة ، وقيل للموصى لهم صدّقوه فيما شئتم ، فإذا أقروا بمقدار فقُلتُ ذلك المقدار يكون في حقهم، وهو ثلث المال، وما بقى من الثُّلُثِ فللموصَى لهم. فلان وادَّعى شيئاً فأعطوه من مالي ما شاء، وهذه معتبرة من الثلث ؛ فلهذا يصدق على الثلث دون الزيادة. كذا في «الهداية»).
[١]قوله : عزل ثلث لها ... الخ ؛ لأنَّ الوصايا حقوق معلومة في الثلث، والميراث معلوم في الثلثين، وهذا الإقرار ليس بدين معلوم ولا وصيّة معلومة، فلا يزاحم المعلوم، فقدمنا عزل المعلوم. كذا في «الرد المحتار) (۲) ناقلاً عن الزيلعي (۳).
[٢] قوله : فلهم ؛ أي للموصى لهم، فإن قيل : قوله : لفلان علي دين، فصدقوه إقرار بدين، والدين مقدم على حق الورثة ، وحق أصحاب الوصايا ، فَلِمَ قدم العزل لهما عليه.
قلنا : الدين إن كان مقدَّماً على الحقين إلا أنه مجهول، وطريق تعينه ما ذكر من تصديق الفريقين.
(۳) قوله : بثلثي ما أقروا به ؛ لأنه إذا أقرّ كلّ فريق بسهم ظهر أنّ في التركةِ ديناً شائعاً في النصيبين، فيؤخذ الدين منهم بحساب ما في أيديهم من التركة. كذا في «الردّ المحتار) ناقلا عن العينيه وغيره.
[٤]قوله : فللموصى لهم ؛ حتى لو قال : الموصى لهم الدين مئة ، يعطى المقر له ثلثها مما في أيديهم، فإن فضل شيءٌ فلهم، وإلا فلا. كذا في «الردّ المحتار).
Book of Bequests / Its Definition and Rulings. And if someone has a debt owed to him, then believe him; he is believed up to one-third. The share of Zayd and Amr are equal, and another has been made a partner with them, so he is a partner for the two, so he has one-third of what each of them has, and this is not possible in the second picture because the shares of Zayd and Amr differ, so he is a partner for each, so he has half of what each of them has. (And if someone has a debt owed to him, then believe him; he is believed up to one-third): meaning they are commanded to believe the creditor regarding the amount of the debt; they must believe him up to one-third. The origin of the right is debt, and its amount is established by way of bequest, and this is istihsan. In qiyas, he would not be believed because the claimant is not believed without proof. [1] L: For if they are more than that, then they are partners in the one-third, so males and females are equal in the one-third. So in the first picture, the share of Zayd and Amr are equal, and another has been made a partner with them, so he is a partner for the two, so he has one-third of what each of them has, due to the unity of the estate. So the other gets three hundred, which is sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams, like each of Zayd and Amr. Contrary to the second picture, because such a difference in the shares of Zayd and Amr is not possible, so he has half of what each of them has, which is seventy-five; because Zayd had one hundred, and half of it is fifty, and Amr had fifty, and half of it is twenty-five, so Zayd and Amr get twenty-five dirhams each. [1] His statement: 'he is not believed' because the acknowledgement of an unknown thing, although valid, is not judged except by clarification. And his statement: 'so believe him' came contrary to Shari'ah, because the claimant is not believed without proof. So commanding to believe the claimant without proof is contrary to Shari'ah, so establishing this acknowledgement as an absolute acknowledgement is impossible, so it is not considered. The face of istihsan: We know that his intention is to give him priority over the heirs, and it is possible to execute his intention by way of bequest. And one who knows the original right against him without its amount may need it in striving to free his conscience. So by making it a bequest, the estimation is given to the legatee, as if he said: 'If someone comes to you claiming something, then give him from my property whatever he wishes.' Then if he also makes a bequest, one-third is set aside for it, and two-thirds for the heirs. And it is said to each: believe him in whatever you wish. And the one entitled to one-third is taken by one-third of what they acknowledged, and what remains is for them (the legatees?). And the heirs are taken by two-thirds of what they acknowledged, and each swears on knowledge of the claim of increase. (Then if he also makes a bequest, one-third is set aside for it, and two-thirds for the heirs. And it is said to each: believe him in whatever you wish. And the one entitled to one-third is taken by one-third of what they acknowledged, and what remains is for them, and the heirs are taken by two-thirds of what they acknowledged, and each swears on knowledge of the claim of increase): meaning, along with that debt whose amount is commanded to be believed, he bequeaths one-third of his property to some people. One-third of the property is set aside for the bequest, and two-thirds for the heirs, and it is said to the legatees: believe him in whatever you wish. If they acknowledge an amount, then that amount is in their right, and it is one-third of the property, and what remains of the one-third is for the legatees. For example, someone claims something, and they give him from my property whatever he wishes. This is considered from the one-third; therefore he is believed regarding the one-third, not beyond. This is from Al-Hidayah. [1] His statement: 'set aside one-third for it... etc.' because bequests are known rights in the one-third, and inheritance is known in the two-thirds, and this acknowledgement is neither a known debt nor a known bequest, so it does not compete with the known, so we prioritized the setting aside of the known. This is from Radd al-Muhtar, quoting from al-Zayla'i. [2] His statement: 'for them' i.e. for the legatees. If it is said: His statement: 'So-and-so has a debt against me, so believe him' is an acknowledgement of a debt, and debt takes precedence over the right of the heirs and the right of the legatees. So why was the setting aside for them (heirs and legatees) given priority over it? We say: The debt, even though it takes precedence over both rights, is unknown, and the way to specify it is what was mentioned of the acknowledgement of the two groups. (3) His statement: 'by two-thirds of what they acknowledged' because when each group acknowledges a share, it appears that in the estate there is a debt diffused in the two portions, so the debt is taken from them according to what is in their hands of the estate. This is from Radd al-Muhtar, quoting from al-Ayni and others. [4] His statement: 'for the legatees' so that if the legatees say: the debt is one hundred, he (the creditor) is given one-third of it from what is in their hands; if anything remains, it is for them, otherwise not. This is from Radd al-Muhtar.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Bequests (Kitab al-Wasaya) discussing how to handle an acknowledged debt when the testator has also made bequests. The author first states the ruling: if a person has a debt owed to him (i.e., the testator owes him), and the heirs are told to believe him, they must believe him up to one-third of the estate. This is not because of a definitive proof from Quran or Sunnah, but based on istihsan (juristic preference). The alternative qiyas would not allow such belief because a claimant is not normally believed without evidence. The reason for istihsan is that the testator's intention is to give this creditor priority over the heirs, and since he can only dispose of one-third via bequests, this arrangement effectively treats the debt as a bequest from the testator. The passage then discusses a scenario where there are also explicit bequests. In that case, one-third is set aside for the bequests, two-thirds for the heirs, and both groups are told to acknowledge the debt proportionally. The creditor gets part of each group's share according to their acknowledgement. The commentary clarifies that the debt is unknown and therefore does not take automatic precedence over known bequests and inheritances; rather, it is settled by the acknowledgement of the parties. It also mentions that each party must swear knowledge if they claim an increase. The legal unit is continuous from the main ruling to the detailed application with numerical examples and comments from later authorities like Al-Hidayah, Radd al-Muhtar, and al-Zayla'i.

Key Terms
وصية (waṣiyyah): A bequest made by a testator, valid only up to one-third of the estate.
دين (dayn): A debt owed by the testator, which is a claim against the estate.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion a testator can dispose of via bequests without heir consent.
إقرار (iqrār): An acknowledgement of a debt or right; here, the heirs' acknowledgement of the creditor's claim.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) for a more suitable ruling.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here, the strict analogy that would not allow believing the claimant without proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, how much of the estate must the heirs believe the creditor's claim up to?
A) The full amount claimed
B) Up to one-third of the estate
C) Up to one-half of the estate
D) The amount left after bequests

Key Takeaway
An uncertain debt acknowledged by a testator is treated as a bequest, limiting the heirs' liability to one-third and requiring proportional contribution from explicit bequests and inheritances.

intermediate

Heir's Acknowledgment of Bequest: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling on heir's acknowledgment of bequest after division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for an heir's acknowledgment of a bequest after division and distinguish it from the analogous ruling of Zufar using istihsan.

Core Idea
An heir who acknowledges a bequest after division pays one-third of his share under istihsan, not half as strict qiyas would require.

Imagine two sons have already divided their father's estate. One son later admits that his father had bequeathed one-third of the entire estate to a third party. How much must this son pay? The Hanafi school, using juristic preference (istihsan), rules that he pays one-third of his own share. This differs from strict analogy (qiyas), which would require him to pay half. In this lesson, we will explore the reasoning behind both views and see why istihsan prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the Hanafi ruling
Two sons divided the estate; one acknowledges a bequest of one-third. The Hanafi ruling (from the passage) is that he pays one-third of his share. Note the key terms: iqrar (acknowledgment), wasiyya (bequest), thuluth (one-third).
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand Zufar's qiyas
Zufar argues using qiyas: acknowledging one-third of the whole estate implies that the estate should be divided into three equal shares. Since one son's share is absent or denied, the remaining two shares are split equally, so the acknowledger gives half of what he holds.
Qiyas here is based on the idea of equality from acknowledgment.
3
Examine the istihsan rationale
Istihsan considers that the acknowledgment is of a one-third share (thuluth shai'i) in the undivided estate. The acknowledger only controls half the estate, so he is effectively acknowledging one-third of what is in his hand (i.e., one-third of his half).
Istihsan departs from strict qiyas for equity.
4
Distinguish from debt acknowledgment
The passage notes that if the acknowledgment were for a debt (not a bequest), the full debt would be paid from the acknowledger's share. The distinction is based on the nature of the claim.
Debt takes priority and is paid fully by the acknowledging heir.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Zufar's view, the legatee receives half of the acknowledger's share; under the Hanafi view, he receives one-third. This is the practical legal consequence of the dispute.
The difference is one-sixth of the total estate in this example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن أقر أحد الابنين بعد القسمة بوصيّة أبيه بالثلث دَفَعَ ثُلُثَ نصيبه) ، هذا عندنا ، والقياس أن يعطيه نصف ما في يده ، وهو قولُ زُفَرَ ؛ لأن إقراره بالثلث يوجب مساواته إياه، وجه الاستحسان : أنه أقرّ بثلث شائع، فيكون مقراً بثلث ما في يده.
[1] قوله : فإن أقر... الخ ؛ توضيحه اقتسم الابنان تركة الأب ثم أقر أحدهما لرجل أنّ أباه أوصى له بثلث ماله دفع المقرّ ثلث نصيبه له. (2) قوله : لأن إقراره ... الخ ؛ يعني أن في زعم المقر أن المال يقسم أثلاثاً ونصيب الموصى له ونصيبُ كلّ واحدٍ من الابنين سواء ، فلَمَّا أنكر أحدهما أو غابَ جُعِلَ كأنّ نصيبه لم يكن ، فيقسم الباقي عليهما نصفين ؛ لأنَّ نصيبهما سواء. كذا «غاية البيان». [3]قوله : ووجه الاستحسان : أنه أقرّ بثلث شائع ؛ في التركة التي نصفها في يدِ المقر ونصفها في يد غيره، فيكون مقراً بثلث ما في يده، بخلاف ما إذا أقر أحد الابنين بدين لغيره، فإنه يقضي للمقر له بكل الدين من نصيب المقر، ووجه الفرق في «غاية البيان».
If one of the two sons, after the division, acknowledges a bequest of one-third by his father, he pays one-third of his share. This is according to us. And by analogy (qiyas) he should give him half of what is in his hand, which is the saying of Zufar, because his acknowledgment of one-third necessitates equality. The face of istihsan is that he acknowledged a one-third share, so he is acknowledging one-third of what is in his hand. [1] His saying: 'If...' etc. Explanation: The two sons divided the father's estate, then one of them acknowledged to a man that his father bequeathed one-third of his property; the acknowledging son pays one-third of his share. (2) His saying: 'Because his acknowledgment...' etc. Meaning: In the view of the acknowledger, the property is divided into three parts: the legatee's share and each son's share are equal. When one of them denies or is absent, it is as if his share did not exist, so the remainder is divided between them in half, because their shares are equal. Thus in 'Ghayat al-Bayan'. [3] His saying: 'The face of istihsan: that he acknowledged a one-third share' in the estate, half of which is in the hand of the acknowledger and half in the hand of another, so he is acknowledging one-third of what is in his hand, unlike if one of the two sons acknowledges a debt to another, then the entire debt is paid from the acknowledger's share. The distinction is explained in 'Ghayat al-Bayan'.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific ruling in the law of bequests (wasaya). The scenario: two sons have already divided their father's estate. After the division, one son admits that his father had made a bequest of one-third of the entire estate to a third party. The question is: how much must this acknowledging son pay to the legatee? The text gives the Hanafi ruling: he pays one-third of his own share. The author contrasts this with qiyas (analogy), which would require him to give half of what is in his hand (because the acknowledger's statement implies the estate should be divided into three equal parts, and since one son's share is absent or denied, the remaining portion should be split equally). This qiyas is attributed to Imam Zufar, a prominent Hanafi jurist. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) instead: the acknowledgment is of a one-third share of the estate, which is undivided (shai'i). Since the acknowledger only controls half the estate, he is effectively acknowledging one-third of what he holds (i.e., one-third of his half). The commentary clarifies that this differs from acknowledgment of a debt, where the acknowledger would bear the full debt. The distinction is explained in detail in 'Ghayat al-Bayan'.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession; here, an heir's admission of a bequest made by the deceased.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest or will; a disposition of property to take effect after death.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third; the maximum fraction of the estate that can be bequeathed without heirs' permission.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here, the opposing view by Zufar based on equality of shares.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from strict analogy for a more equitable result.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half of his share
B) One-third of his share
C) Half of the entire estate
D) One-third of the entire estate

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an heir's acknowledgment of a bequest after division is treated by istihsan, requiring payment of one-third of his share, not half.
