Bequest of a Pregnant Slave: Mother and Child (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on allocation of bequest of pregnant slave who gives birth after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa’s and the Sahibayn’s allocation of a bequeathed pregnant slave who gives birth after death, and apply the principle “al-tabi’ la yuzahim al-asl”.

Core Idea
The dependent child does not compete with the mother in a bequest; Abu Hanifa prioritizes the original, the Sahibayn allocate proportionally.

When a testator bequeaths a pregnant slave and she gives birth after his death, the newborn is included as a dependent of the bequest. However, the Hanafi masters differ on how to allocate the bequest between mother and child when their combined value exceeds one-third. Abu Hanifa insists that the original subject (the mother) is prioritized, while his two students apply proportional distribution. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal problem
A testator bequeaths a specific pregnant female slave. She gives birth after his death but before the estate is divided. The combined value of mother and child exceeds one-third of the estate. How should the bequest be satisfied?
The key timing: birth before division. If after division, the child belongs solely to the legatee.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the legatee takes the mother first, and only uses the child to make up any shortfall in the one-third limit. The mother is the original subject (asl); the child is dependent (tabi‘).
The principle: al-tabi‘ la yuzahim al-asl (the dependent does not compete with the original).
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the bequest applies proportionally to both mother and child. The legatee takes a fraction of each according to their values. The child, having entered the bequest as dependent, remains covered after birth.
They analogize to sale and manumission, where a child born to a sold/freed slave is included.
4
Analyze the proofs behind each view
Abu Hanifa's proof: executing the bequest equally on both would invalidate part of the original bequest (the mother), which is impermissible. The Sahibayn's proof: the bequest extends (yusra) to increments, as established in other contracts.
Abu Hanifa distinguishes from sale: in sale, the contract remains valid even if a dependent consumes part of the price; in bequest, the disposal of property is more restricted.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In the given example, both methods result in the same total value (400) but different composition: under Abu Hanifa, the legatee receives the whole mother (300) and one-third of the child (100); under the Sahibayn, two-thirds of each (200+200). The difference matters when the values are not symmetric or when the one-third limit is smaller.
The text does not explicitly prefer one view; both are recorded in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن وَلَدَتِ الموصى بها بعد موته فهما له : أي الأمة الموصى بها وولدها، إن خرجا من الثلث وإلا أخذ الثلث منها ، ثمّ منه) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له؛ لأن التبع لا يزاحم الأصل، وعندهما يأخذ من كلِّ واحد بالحصة ، فإذا كان له ستمئة درهم، وأمة تساوي ثلثمئة، فولدت ولدا يساوي ثلثمئة درهم بعد موتِ الموصى حتى صار مالُهُ ألفاً ومئتين، فثُلُثُ المال أربعمئة ، فعند أبي حنيفة للموصى له الأم، وثُلث الولد" ، وعندهما ثلثا كل منهما.
[1] قوله : لا يزاحم الأصل؛ فيأخذ الموصى له ذلك الثلث من الأم، فإن نقص شيء من الثلث أخذه من الولد. [۲] قوله : فإذا كان... الخ ; قال في «الهداية» (۱) : في «الجامع الصغير»: عين صورة ، وقال رجل له ستمئة درهم وأمةٌ تساوي ثلاثمئة درهم، فأوصى بالجارية لرجل ثم مات ، فولدت ولداً يساوي ثلاثمئة درهم قبل القسمة، فللموصى له الأم وثلث الولد عنده، وعندهما له ثلثا كل واحد منهما. لهما: ما ذكرنا من أنّ الولد دخل في الوصية تبعاً حالة الاتصال، فلا يخرج عنها بالانفصال، كما في البيع والعتق ، فتنفذ الوصيّة فيهما على السواء من غير تقديم الأم. وله : إن الأم أصل والولد تبع فيه، والتبعُ لا يزاحم الأصل، فلو نفذنا الوصية فيهما جميعاً تنتقض الوصية في بعض الأصل، وذلك لا يجوز بخلاف البيع ; لأنَّ تنفيذ البيع في البيع لا يؤدي إلى نقضه في الأصل. بل يبقى تاماً صحيحاً فيه إلا أنه لا يقابله بعض الثمن ضرورة مقابلته بالولد، فاسداً. از إذا اتصل به القبض، ولكن الثمن تابع في البيع، حتى ينعقد البيع بدون ذكره، وإن كان ا. انتهى. وإنما قال : فولدت قبل القسمة ; لأنه إذا ولدت بعد القسمة فهو للموصي له ; لأنه نماء خالص ملكه ; لتقرّر ملكه فيه بعد القسمة. (٣) قوله : الأم وثلث الولد ; وهو المئة، فالمجموع أربعمئة ; لأن الأمة والولد فرض كلّ واحدٍ منهما مساوي ثلاثمئة درهم، وعندهما: ثلثا كل منهما، فالمجموع أربعمئة أيضاً. [٤] قوله : وعندهما ثلثا كل منهما ; لأنَّ الوصية تسري إلى الزوائد الحادثة قبل القسمة، بل إجماع لكون الشركة باقية على ملك الميت، وإذا ثبت السراية صار كأنَّ الوصية وقعت بهما . هكذا في الجلبي
If the bequeathed slave-woman gives birth after his death, both (her and her child) belong to the legatee, if they come out of one-third; otherwise, he takes one-third from her, then from him (the child). This is according to Abu Hanifa, because the dependent does not compete with the original. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he takes proportionally from each. For example: if he had six hundred dirhams and a slave-woman worth three hundred, and she gave birth to a child worth three hundred dirhams after the testator's death, so his estate became one thousand two hundred; one-third is four hundred. According to Abu Hanifa, the legatee gets the mother and one-third of the child; according to the two, he gets two-thirds of each. [1] His saying: 'Does not compete with the original'; the legatee takes that one-third from the mother; if anything is lacking from the one-third, he takes it from the child. [2] His saying: 'If... etc.' He said in al-Hidayah: in al-Jami' al-Saghir, a specific example: a man had six hundred dirhams and a slave-woman worth three hundred; he bequeathed the slave-woman to a man, then died; she gave birth to a child worth three hundred dirhams before division. According to him (Abu Hanifa), the legatee gets the mother and one-third of the child; according to the two, he gets two-thirds of each. The two's argument: the child entered the bequest as dependent when attached, so it does not leave by separation, as in sale and manumission; thus the bequest applies equally to both without prioritizing the mother. His argument: the mother is the original and the child is dependent, and the dependent does not compete with the original; if we executed the bequest on both, the bequest would be invalidated in part of the original, which is not allowed, unlike sale, because execution of sale does not lead to its invalidation in the original. Rather, it remains completely valid, but part of the price is not received due to the child, becoming invalid if possession is taken, but the price is dependent in sale, so the sale is concluded without mentioning it, etc. End. He only said 'gave birth before division' because if she gave birth after division, it belongs to the legatee, as it is pure profit of his ownership, due to the establishment of his ownership after division. (3) His saying: 'the mother and one-third of the child'; that is one hundred, so total four hundred; because the mother and child are each valued at three hundred; according to the two: two-thirds of each, total also four hundred. [4] His saying: 'according to the two, two-thirds of each'; because the bequest extends to the increments occurring before division, indeed by consensus since the joint ownership remains on the deceased's property; when extension is established, it is as if the bequest occurred on both. Thus in al-Jalabi.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a testator bequeaths a specific pregnant slave-woman (or any female slave), and she gives birth after his death but before the estate is divided. The ruling concerns the distribution of the bequest between the mother and the newborn. The Hanafi imams differ: Abu Hanifa holds that the mother (the original subject of the bequest) is prioritized, and the child (dependent) is secondary. The legatee takes the mother first; if her value exceeds one-third, he takes only one-third of her, and if the one-third is not fully used, he takes from the child. In contrast, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the bequest applies proportionally to both, as if the bequest was made on both jointly, because the child is an increment that follows the mother and remains covered by the bequest. The example illustrates: the deceased has 600 dirhams plus a slave worth 300 (total 900?), but after death the child adds 300, making total 1200. One-third is 400. Under Abu Hanifa: mother (300) belongs to legatee fully, plus 100 from the child (since 300+100=400). Under the two: legatee takes two-thirds of each, i.e., 200 from mother and 200 from child (total 400). Both views arrive at the same total but differ in how it is allocated. The reasoning: Abu Hanifa emphasizes the principle that 'the dependent does not compete with the original' (al-tabi' la yuzahim al-asl). The two argue that since the child was attached at the time of the bequest, it is included as a dependent and remains included after separation, analogous to sale or manumission where a child born to a sold or freed slave-woman is included. The commentary further clarifies that if the birth occurs after division (i.e., after the legatee has taken possession), the child belongs entirely to the legatee as profit of his already established ownership.

Key Terms
أمة (ama): A female slave; the subject of the bequest.
ولد (walad): Child born after the testator's death; considered an increment (namā') of the bequeathed property.
تبع (tabi'): Dependent or accessory; the child is dependent on the mother for the purpose of the bequest.
أصل (asl): Original; the mother as the primary subject of the bequest.
سراية (sarayan): Extension of the legal effect to dependent matters; here, the bequest extends to the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The legatee takes the mother and the child proportionally
B) The legatee takes the mother first, and only then the child to make up the one-third
C) The legatee takes only the mother and none of the child
D) The legatee takes only the child and none of the mother

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the dependent child is included in a bequest of a pregnant slave, but Abu Hanifa prioritizes the mother as the original, while the Sahibayn allocate proportionally between mother and child.

Priority Between Manumission and Muhiba in Marad al-Mawt
Intra-Hanafi dispute on priority between itq and muhiba in wasaya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding priority between manumission (itq) and preferential treatment (muhiba) in a sick person's will and apply the mufta bihi position to a given scenario.

Core Idea
In a sick person's will, manumission is irrevocable, but preferential treatment derives strength from being part of a sale contract.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi debate. When a terminally ill person both manumits a slave and gives preferential treatment (selling undervalue) to another, both acts are treated as wills subject to the one-third limit. But which takes priority if they compete? The classic dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hinges on the nature of each act: manumission is irrevocable, while muhiba is embedded in a commutative contract. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi ta'lil and tarjih in complex wasaya cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Act
Recognize that both manumission (itq) and preferential treatment (muhiba) during marad al-mawt are treated as bequests (wasaya), subject to the one-third rule.
This is the foundational premise from which the dispute arises.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that muhiba is stronger when it occurs first because it is part of a commutative contract (mu'awada); if itq occurs first, itq takes precedence because it cannot be rescinded.
Timing and the contractual nature are key.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that itq always takes priority because it is irrevocable (cannot be rescinded), regardless of order.
They emphasize the permanence of manumission.
4
Analyze the Proofs (Ta'lil)
Compare the effective causes: Abu Hanifa sees strength in muhiba due to its contractual context; Sahibayn see strength in itq due to its irrevocability.
This is a classic ta'lil divergence.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The distribution of the one-third among competing acts differs: under Abu Hanifa, priority depends on order; under Sahibayn, itq always takes the largest share.
The mufta bihi is Sahibayn's view, so in practice itq is favored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومرض صح منه كالصحة، وإعتاقه ومحاباته وهبته وضمانه وصية، فإن حابي فأعتق، فهي أحق، وهما في عكسه سواء. وقالا: عنقه أولى فيهما، ففي عتقه بين المحاباتين نصف للأولى ونصف للآخرين، وفي محاباة بين عتقين، لها نصف الثلث ولهما نصف، والعتق أولى عندهما فيهما. ثم باع العبد الذي قيمته مئتان بمئة، يقسم الثلث وهو المئة بينهما نصفين، فالعبد المعتق يعتق نصفه مجاناً، ويسعى في نصف قيمته، وصاحب المحاباة يأخذ العبد الآخر بمئة وخمسين. وقالا: عتقه أولى فيهما؛ لأنه لا يلحقه الفسخ. له: أن المحاباة أقوى؛ لأنه في ضمن عقد المعاوضة، لكن إن وجد العتق أولاً، وهو لا يحتمل الدفع، فيزاحم المحاباة. ففي عتقه بين المحاباتين نصف للأولى ونصف للآخرين، وفي محاباة بين عتقين، لها نصف الثلث ولهما نصف، والعتق أولى عندهما فيهما.
And sickness that recovers from is like health. And his manumission, preferential treatment, gift, guarantee, and will [are like a will]. If he gave preferential treatment and then manumitted, it [the preferential treatment] is more entitled, and both are equal in its opposite. And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: his manumission is more entitled in both. So in his manumission between two preferential treatments: half for the first and half for the others; and in preferential treatment between two manumissions: for it half of the third and for them half, and manumission is more entitled according to them. Then he sold the slave whose value is two hundred for one hundred; he divides the third, which is one hundred, between them in halves; so the manumitted slave is freed half for free and he works for half his value; and the owner of the preferential treatment takes the other slave for one hundred and fifty. And they two said: his manumission is more entitled in both because recission does not affect it. To him (Abu Hanifa): that preferential treatment is stronger because it is within a commutative contract, but if manumission occurs first and it does not admit repelling, then it competes with preferential treatment. So in his manumission between two preferential treatments: half for the first and half for the others; and in preferential treatment between two manumissions: for it half of the third and for them half, and manumission is more entitled according to them.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the priority between manumission (itq) and preferential treatment (muhiba) when they compete for the one-third limit in a sick person's will. The base text states that if a sick person gives preferential treatment (sells undervalue) then manumits, the preferential treatment takes precedence; if the reverse, both are equal. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) counter that manumission is always more entitled in both scenarios because manumission is irrevocable (cannot be rescinded), whereas preferential treatment is part of a sale contract which can be rescinded. Abu Hanifa argues that preferential treatment is stronger because it is embedded in a commutative contract (mu'awada), but if manumission occurs first, it takes priority because it cannot be repelled. The practical outcome is illustrated with examples: when manumission occurs between two preferential treatments, the third is split half to the first preferential treatment and half to the second, with the manumission competing proportionally. In the reverse, the preferential treatment gets half the third and the two manumissions share the other half. This dispute shows the Hanafi method of ta'lil (identifying effective cause) and tarjih (preference).

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): Selling an item below its market value (preferential treatment) during marad al-mawt, treated as a will.
عتق (ʿitq): Manumission of a slave by the owner, which in marad al-mawt is also considered a will.
الثلث (ath-thuluth): The one-third of the estate that a sick person can dispose of through wills and gratuitous acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is muhiba (preferential treatment) considered stronger than itq when it occurs first?
A) Because itq can be rescinded easily.
B) Because muhiba is within a commutative contract and thus more binding.
C) Because muhiba involves a price payment.
D) Because the Prophet (saw) recommended muhiba.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, manumission (itq) is always given priority over preferential treatment (muhiba) when competing for the one-third limit in a sick person's will.

Precedence of Manumission over Muhabah in Bequests
Intra-Hanafi dispute on priority between manumission and preferential dealing in wasaya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Sahibayn prioritize manumission over muhabah and state the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Manumission takes precedence in bequests because it cannot be rescinded – a stronger legal effect than muhabah.

When a dying person makes multiple bequests that exceed one-third, Hanafi jurists rank them. This lesson examines a specific conflict: manumission (atq) versus preferential dealing (muhabah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Abu Hanifa differ on which is stronger. The passage presents their arguments and a worked example.

Guided Path
1
State the conflict
Identify the two types of bequest competing within the one-third: manumission of a slave (atq) and preferential dealing in a sale (muhabah).
Muhabah is a discount given by the seller, treated as a bequest from the one-third.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds that muhabah is stronger and should be prioritized; the Sahibayn hold that manumission takes precedence in both cases.
The Sahibayn's view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
3
Extract the proof for each
Sahibayn argue that manumission cannot be rescinded (faskh), making it more binding. Abu Hanifa argues that muhabah is part of a contract of exchange (mu'awada), which can be rescinded, but if manumission occurs first, it contends.
The key illa (effective cause) for Sahibayn is the absence of rescission.
4
Apply the numerical example
The text gives an example: a slave worth 200 is sold for 100 (muhabah discount). The third is 100. Divide 100 equally between manumission and muhabah. The manumitted slave is freed half and works for half his value; the muhabah recipient takes the other slave for 150.
The example illustrates how the one-third is allocated under the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, muhabah would receive a larger share; under the Sahibayn, manumission is prioritized. The practical outcome differs depending on which position is followed.
The mufta bihi view (Sahibayn) gives manumission priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالا : عنقه أولى فيهما ، ففي عتقه بين المحاباتين نصف للأولى ونصف للآخرين، وفي محاباة بين عتقين، لها نصفُ الثلث، ولهما نصف، والعتق أولى عندهما فيهما ثُمَّ باع العبد الذي قيمته مئتان بمئةٍ ، يَقْسِمُ الثُّلث، وهو المئة بينهما نصفين، فالعبد المعتق يُعتق نصفه مجاناً، ويسعى في نصف قيمته، وصاحب المحاباة يأخذ العبد الآخر بمئة وخمسين، وقالا : عتقه أولى فيهما ) ؛ لأنه لا يلحقه الفسخ . له : أن المحاباة أقوى ؛ لأنه في ضمن عقدِ المعاوضة، لكن إن وُجِدَ العتقُ أولاً، ، وهو لا يحتمل الدفع، فيزاحم المحاباة. ففي عتقه بين المحاباتين نصف للأولى ونصف للآخرين، وفي محاباة بين عتقين ، لها نصفُ الثَّلث ولهما نصف والعتق أولى عندهما فيهما.
And they both said: His manumission takes precedence in both cases. So in the case of his manumission between two preferential dealings, half is for the first and half for the others. And in the case of a preferential dealing between two manumissions, she has half the third, and they have half, and manumission takes precedence according to them both in both cases. Then he sold the slave whose value was two hundred for one hundred: he divides the third, which is one hundred, between them in halves. So the manumitted slave is freed half for free, and he works for half his value. And the owner of the preferential dealing takes the other slave for one hundred and fifty. And they both said: his manumission takes precedence in both cases, because it is not subject to rescission. He (Abu Hanifa) said: Preferential dealing is stronger because it is within a contract of exchange, but if manumission occurs first, and it does not bear repulsion, then it contends with the preferential dealing. So in his manumission between the two preferential dealings, half is for the first and half for the others. And in a preferential dealing between two manumissions, she has half the third and they have half, and manumission takes precedence according to them both in both cases.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the allocation of the one-third bequest when multiple bequests compete, specifically between manumission (atq) and preferential dealing (muhabah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that manumission is given priority in both scenarios because manumission, once executed, cannot be rescinded. In contrast, Abu Hanifa argues that muhabah is stronger because it is part of a contract of exchange (mu'awada) which can be rescinded, but if manumission occurs first, it cannot be undone, so it contends. The text then provides an example: a slave worth 200 is sold for 100, the third is 100, divided equally between the manumission and the muhabah. Then the manumitted slave is half freed and works for his value, while the muhabah recipient gets the other slave for 150. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view, as manumission is a stronger act of devotion.

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): Preferential dealing in a sale where the seller gives a discount to the buyer, treated as a bequest from one-third.
عتق (ʿitq): Manumission of a slave, which is an act of devotion and a bequest from one-third when done at the edge of death (marad al-mawt).
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract. Manumission once executed cannot be rescinded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does manumission take precedence over muhabah in bequests?
A) Because manumission is a stronger form of worship.
B) Because manumission cannot be rescinded, unlike muhabah.
C) Because manumission is always for a specific slave.
D) Because muhabah is not a valid bequest.

Key Takeaway
Manumission is prioritized over muhabah in bequests because it cannot be rescinded, making it more binding.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Bequest of Manumission with Specific Sum – Partial Loss
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of manumission bequest when part of specified sum is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a bequest of manumission with a specific sum when part is lost, and explain the underlying principle that drives the difference.

Core Idea
A bequest to free a slave with a set sum: if the sum shrinks, does the bequest fail? It depends on who owns the right.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about bequests. Imagine a person bequeaths 100 dirhams to buy and free a slave. Before execution, some money is lost. Does the executor free a cheaper slave or is the bequest void? Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. The answer hinges on whether manumission is a right of Allah or a right of the slave.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the issue
A testator bequeaths that a slave be bought and freed using a specified sum (e.g., 100 dirhams). Part of that sum is lost. Is the manumission executed with the remainder?
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa: the bequest fails for the remainder. Reason: the act of worship (freeing a slave) varies with the slave's value. The bequest is for a specific slave of that value; freeing a cheaper one changes the intended recipient.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Sahibayn: the bequest is executed with the remainder, analogous to Hajj bequest. Reason: both are acts of worship (qurbah) and should be implemented as fully as possible. The entitlement does not change.
4
Analyze the underlying principle
Abu Hanifa views manumission as a right of the slave (so the mustahiq changes with the slave). Sahibayn view it as a right of Allah (so the mustahiq is unchanged). This is based on a different rule about accepting testimony.
Al-Hidayah mentions this principle as crucial.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the thamarah
The Sahibayn's view is considered more appropriate (as per al-Hidayah) and is the operative position for fatwa. The practical consequence: if the testator bequeathed 100 dirhams for manumission and 10 are lost, the executor still frees a slave but with the remaining 90; under Abu Hanifa, the bequest would be void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووصيته بأن يعتق عنه بهذه المئة عبد لا ينفذ بما بقي إن هلك درهم بخلاف الحج، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما ينفذ العتق بما بقي كما في الحج. له : إن القربة تتفاوت بتفاوت قيمة العبد بخلاف الحج. توضيحه من أوصى بأن يعتق عنه بهذه المئة عبد؛ أي يشترى بهذه المئة عبد ويعتق عن الموصي، فهلك منها درهم، لم يعتق عنه بما بقي عند أبي حنيفة. بخلاف الحج؛ أي إن أوصى بأن يحج عنه بهذه المئة فهلك منها درهم يحج عنه بما بقي. وعندهما ينفذ العتق بما بقي؛ كما في الحج؛ لأنه وصية بنوع قربة، فيجب تنفيذها مهما أمكن اعتبارا بالوصية بالحج. وله : إنه وصية بالعتق لعبد يشترى بمئة وتنفيذها فيمن يشترى بأقل منه تنفيذ لغير الموصى له؛ لأن القربة يتفاوت بتفاوت قيمة العبد، وذلك لا يجوز بخلاف الوصية بالحج؛ لأنها قربة محضة هي حق الله تعالى، والمستحق لم يتبدل، وصارت هذه الوصية كما إذا أوصى لرجل بمئة فهلك بعضها، يدفع الباقي إليه. قال في الهداية: قيل هذه المسألة بناءً على أصل آخر مختلف فيه، وهو أن العتق حق الله تعالى عندهما، حتى تقبل الشهادة عليه من غير دعوى، فلم يتبدل المستحق، وعنده حق العبد حتى لا تقبل البينة عليه من غير دعوى، فاختلف المستحق. وهذا أشبه. انتهى. إن القربة... يعني الموصي صرح بذلك، فصار الموصى له عبداً قيمته مئة لا من قيمته أقل منها. كذا في الجلبي.
And his bequest that a slave be freed for him with this hundred is not executed with what remains if a dirham is lost, unlike Hajj. This according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And according to them (the Sahibayn), manumission is executed with what remains just as in Hajj. He (Abu Hanifa) argued: The act of worship varies with the variation of the slave's value, unlike Hajj. Explanation: When one bequeaths that a slave be freed for him with this hundred, meaning a slave is bought with this hundred and freed on behalf of the testator, and a dirham of it is lost, then according to Abu Hanifa the slave is not freed with what remains. Unlike Hajj: if he bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him with this hundred and a dirham is lost, then Hajj is performed with what remains. According to them (the Sahibayn), manumission is executed with what remains just as in Hajj, because it is a bequest for a type of devotion, so it must be executed as much as possible by analogy to the bequest for Hajj. And according to him (Abu Hanifa): This is a bequest for manumission of a slave bought for a hundred, and executing it for someone bought for less is executing for someone other than the legatee, because the act of worship varies with the variation of the slave's value, and that is not permissible, unlike the bequest for Hajj because it is pure devotion that is a right of Allah, and the one entitled does not change. And this bequest becomes like when someone bequeaths to a man a hundred dirhams and some of it is lost: the remainder is given to him. It is said in al-Hidayah: This issue is based on another disputed principle, which is that manumission is a right of Allah according to them (the Sahibayn), so testimony regarding it is accepted without claim, so the one entitled does not change. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), it is a right of the slave, so testimony regarding it is not accepted without claim, so the one entitled changes. And this is more akin. End. 'The act of worship...' meaning the testator specified that, so the legatee becomes a slave whose value is a hundred, not one of lesser value. Thus in al-Jalabi.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a bequest to free a slave with a specific sum of money, where part of the sum is lost. Abu Hanifa holds that the bequest is invalidated for the remainder because the act of worship (freeing a slave) varies with the slave's value, so executing it with a reduced amount changes the intended beneficiary. The Sahibayn analogize it to a bequest for Hajj, where a reduction in funds still permits Hajj to be performed with the remainder, as Hajj is a pure act of worship. Abu Hanifa differentiates because the value of the slave matters for the devotion. The text also notes that this dispute is based on a deeper principle: whether manumission is a right of Allah (allowing acceptance of testimony without a claim) or a right of the slave (requiring a claim). The Sahibayn hold the former, making the entitlement unchanged; Abu Hanifa holds the latter, making the entitlement specific to the slave. The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn, as manumission is considered a right of Allah, so the bequest is executed with the remaining amount.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship or devotion that brings one closer to Allah.
تنفيذ (tanfīdh): Execution or implementation of a bequest.
مستحق (mustaḥiqq): The person entitled to the benefit of the bequest. In manumission, it is the slave; in Hajj, it is Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because manumission is not a valid bequest.
B) Because the act of worship (qurbah) varies with the value of the slave, so the bequest is for a specific object.
C) Because the remaining amount is insufficient for any slave.
D) Because the testator did not intend any other slave.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, the difference between viewing manumission as a right of Allah versus a right of the slave decides whether a reduced bequest is executed or void; the Sahibayn's view is relied upon.

When Debt and Manumission Conflict: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Slave’s Work
Intra-Hanafi dispute on slave's work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa requires a slave to work (saiayah) when a debt claim is confirmed by the heir, and state the opposing view of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When claims conflict, the stronger effect on the estate prevails: debt overrides manumission, forcing the slave to work.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the fate of a slave when an heir confirms both a debt and a manumission claimed against the deceased. The core question: does the slave have to work to pay his value, or is he freed immediately? Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to handle conflicting claims in estate matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conflicting Claims
Recognize that one claimant alleges a debt against the deceased, and another alleges that the deceased manumitted a slave during health. The heir confirms both claims.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave must work (saiayah) to pay his value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the slave is freed without any obligation.
3
Analyse Abu Hanifa’s Proof
The debt acknowledgment is stronger because it is paid from the entire estate, whereas manumission during illness is limited to one-third. Since manumission cannot be literally invalidated, it is invalidated in meaning by requiring the slave to work.
Hanafi principe: debt takes precedence over partial manumission.
4
Analyse the Sahibayn’s Proof
Both claims appear together due to the heir’s single confirmation, so they are treated as simultaneous. Manumission during health does not oblige the slave to work.
They treat the timing as concurrent, avoiding overriding one over the other.
5
Examine the Related Deposit Case
The passage also discusses a case where a debt and a deposit are both confirmed. According to al-Hidayah, Abu Hanifa says the deposit is stronger; the Sahibayn say they are equal. However, many earlier authorities recorded the opposite (Sahibayn say deposit stronger, Abu Hanifa says equal). This shows the importance of verifying riwayah.
The teacher’s correction highlights the need for careful transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ادعى رجل ديناً على ميت، وعبده إعتاقه في صحته، وصدقهما وارثه، سعى العبد في قيمته، هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : يعتق، ولا يسعى في شيء؛ لأنَّ الدِّين والعتق في الصحةِ ظهرا معاً بتصديق الوارث في كلام واحد، فصار كأنهما وقعا معا، والعتق في الصحة لا يوجب السعاية . له : أنّ الإقرار بالدين أقوى؛ لأنه في المرض يعتبر من كل المال، والإقرار بالعتق في المرض يعتبر من الثلث، فيجب أن يبطل العتق، لكنه لا يحتمل البطلان، فيبطل معنى بإيجاب السعاية. وعلى هذا الخلاف: إذا مات الرجلُ وترك ألف درهم، فقال رجل : لي علي الميت ألف درهم ديناً، وقال الآخر : كان لي عنده ألف درهم وديعة، فقال الوارث : صدقتما، قال في «الهداية»: فعنده الوديعة أقوى، وعندهما: سواء. قال أستاذ أستاذي أخي المعظم مولانا محمد عبد الحليم أدخله الله في جنات النعيم : هذا من المسامحات ، فإنّ الكبار القدماء ذكروا الخلاف على العكس ، فالحاكم في «مختصر الكافي»، والفقيه أبو الليث في كتاب «مختلف الرواية»، والقُدُوري في کتاب «التقريب»، وفخر الإسلام» في شرح الجامع الصغير»، والصدر الشهيد والإمام نجم الدين النَّسَفِيّ في كتاب «الحصر» وغيرهم قالوا : إنّ عندهما الوديعة أقوى، وعنده سواء. والتفصيل في «غاية البيان».
If a man claims a debt against a deceased, and [claims] his slave was manumitted by him during his health, and their heir confirms both, the slave must work to pay his value. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: He is freed and does not work for anything, because the debt and the manumission during health appear together by the confirmation of the heir in a single statement, so it is as if they occurred together, and manumission during health does not necessitate working. For him [Abu Hanifa]: The acknowledgment of debt is stronger, because during illness it is considered from all the property, and acknowledgment of manumission during illness is considered from one third, so the manumission must be invalidated, but it does not admit invalidation, so it is invalidated in meaning by imposing working. And upon this difference: If a man dies leaving one thousand dirhams, and a man says: 'I have upon the deceased one thousand dirhams as a debt,' and another says: 'He had with me one thousand dirhams as a deposit,' and the heir says: 'You both speak the truth,' then in al-Hidayah it is said: According to him [Abu Hanifa] the deposit is stronger, and according to the two [it is] equal. My teacher's teacher, my respected brother, our master Muhammad Abd al-Halim, may Allah enter him into the gardens of bliss, said: This is from leniency; indeed, the great early scholars mentioned the difference in opposite manner: al-Hakim in Mukhtasar al-Kafi, the jurist Abu al-Layth in Kitab Mukhtalaf al-Riwayah, al-Quduri in Kitab al-Taqrib, Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Sadr al-Shahid, Imam Najm al-Din al-Nasafi in Kitab al-Hasr, and others said: According to the two the deposit is stronger, and according to him it is equal. And the detail is in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 616

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the fate of a slave when an heir confirms both a debt against the deceased and the manumission of the slave during the deceased's health. The text is from a commentary on al-Wiqayah, expanding the ruling. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the slave must work (saiayah) to pay his value to the heirs, because the debt claim overrides the manumission. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the slave is free without obligation, since both claims are confirmed simultaneously, and manumission during health does not entail working. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the acknowledgment of debt is stronger because it affects the entire estate, whereas manumission during illness is limited to one-third; thus the manumission is effectively nullified by requiring the slave to work. The passage then presents a related case: a deceased leaves 1000 dirhams, one claimant says it is a debt, another says it is a deposit, and the heir confirms both. According to al-Hidayah, Abu Hanifa says the deposit is stronger (so the deposit claim prevails), while the Sahibayn say they are equal. However, the author's teacher, Muhammad Abd al-Halim, corrects this, noting that many earlier authorities recorded the opposite: the Sahibayn considered the deposit stronger, and Abu Hanifa considered them equal. This highlights the importance of verifying transmission within the school.

Key Terms
سعاية (saiayah): Working to pay the value of freedom; required of a slave when a debt claim overrides the manumission.
دين (dayn): A financial obligation owed by the deceased to a claimant.
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the manumission becomes void entirely.
B) Because the debt claim is stronger and effectively nullifies the manumission, but manumission cannot be literal void so it is nullified in meaning by requiring working.
C) Because the heir chose to confirm the debt first.
D) Because the slave is still a slave until he pays.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute on conflicting claims, Abu Hanifa prioritizes debt over manumission by imposing work on the slave, while the Sahibayn treat them as simultaneous, freeing the slave immediately.

Bequest to Bani Fulan: Inclusion of Women and Counting Conditions
Ruling on bequest to a named group with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether females are included in a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' and explain the counting condition for group bequests.

Core Idea
Bequest to 'Bani Fulan' includes females only if it is a tribal name; otherwise, only males inherit.

This lesson addresses two intertwined issues in Hanafi bequest law: first, how to classify a bequest to a group that can or cannot be counted; second, whether a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' (sons of so-and-so) includes female descendants. The Ḥanafī school has an internal disagreement on the latter, with the later view restricting it to males unless the wording denotes a tribe or clan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios for group bequests
The passage states that if the group is countable, the bequest is tamlik (individual ownership) for both rich and poor. If uncountable, it becomes qurbah (piety) and is spent only on the poor among them.
The counting condition is defined by later scholars as judge's discretion, with a guideline of about 100 from Imam Muhammad.
2
Analyze the linguistic dispute over 'Bani Fulan'
The early Hanafi view (including Abu Hanifa's first opinion and the Sahibayn) held that the masculine plural includes females. Later, Abu Hanifa retracted, stating it refers only to males, unless the phrase is a tribal name (like Bani Tamim) where it denotes lineage and includes both genders.
The Shafi'i school generally includes females, but the Hanafi school follows the later view.
3
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
For the counting condition, the judge's discretion is the relied-upon position (Fatawa Qadi Khan). For female inclusion, the later view of Abu Hanifa (males only unless tribal) is adopted, as preferred by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
Thus, a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' when Fulan is an individual gives only to males; when it is a tribe, both genders share.
4
Apply the rule to a new example
If someone bequeaths to 'Bani Ahmad' and Ahmad is a known individual (not a tribe), only male descendants inherit. If Ahmad is the founder of a tribe, female descendants also receive a share.
The judge must also decide if the group is countable or uncountable to determine tamlik vs qurbah.

Source Text

في «الكفاية» (۳) : إنّما يدخلُ الإناث تحت هذه الوصيّة فيما إذا اختلط الذكور والإناث ، وأما إذا انفرد الإناث فلا شيء لهن بالاتفاق.
وهذا أي دخولُ الإناث في هذه الوصيّة أوّل قول أبي حنيفة له، وهو قولهما ؛ لأنَّ جمع الذكور يتناول الإناث، ثم رجع وقال : يتناول الذكور خاصة ؛ لأنَّ حقيقة الاسم المذكور وانتظامه للإناث يجوز ، والكلام حقيقة بخلاف ما إذا كان بنو فلان اسم قبيلة أو فخذ، حيث يتناول الذكور والإناث ؛ لأنه ليس يراد بها أعيانهم ؛ إذ هو مجرد الانتساب. كذا في «الهداية»(4).
And in 'Bani Fulan', the female among them. Hasan al-Diraya for the end of Sharh al-Wiqaya. If they are a group that can be counted, both the poor and the rich enter; then it is a possession for them. And if they are a group that cannot be counted, it is not possession for them, rather it is intended as piety, which is in repelling need, so it is spent on the poor among them: i.e., the poor orphans of Bani Zaid, or the poor blind of them, and likewise for the rest. (And in 'Bani Fulan', the female among them. After puberty, it is narrated by Abu Dawud in his Sunan. And because the orphan is an expression of singularity: it is said: a unique pearl, i.e., having no peer, solitary. So whoever is isolated from the one who raises him in a state of needing upbringing is an orphan, and after puberty he is independent of the one who raises him due to his ability to manage his own affairs, so he is not called an orphan. And 'aramil' is the plural of 'armal'. In al-Tahdhib: it is said for the poor person who has no ability for anything, male or female, 'armal', and it is not said for a woman who has no husband and is wealthy that she is an 'armalah'. And al-Sha'bi said: femaleness is not a condition, rather it includes male and female, except that the correct is what Muhammad Allah interpreted that the 'armalah' is an adult woman who had a husband who left her or died from her, whether he consummated or not, and his statement is authoritative in language. And some said: 'armalah' is one who has no husband, and it is not conditional that she had a husband. So in al-Kifayah. [1] His statement: 'a group that can be counted' - its interpretation according to Abu Yusuf is that they can be counted without writing and calculation, and Muhammad said: if they are more than a hundred, they are not countable, and some said: it is delegated to the judge's opinion, and upon it is the fatwa, and what Muhammad said indicates it. So in al-Kifayah, quoting from Fatawa Qadi Khan. [2] His statement: 'And in Bani Fulan... etc.' i.e., if one makes a bequest to Bani Fulan, females enter it. He said: in Sunan Abi Dawud (3:115), etc. Al-Kifayah (9:404-405). Al-Kifayah (4:404-405). Book of Wills / Its definition and rulings. In al-Kifayah: Only the females enter under this bequest when males and females are mixed; but if they are solely females, there is nothing for them by agreement. And this - i.e., the entry of females in this bequest - is the first statement of Abu Hanifa, and it is the statement of the two companions, because the plural of males includes females. Then he retracted and said: it refers specifically to males, because the reality of the mentioned noun and its arrangement for females is permissible, but speech is reality, contrary to if 'Bani Fulan' is the name of a tribe or clan, where it includes males and females, because it is not intended for their individuals; rather it is mere lineage. So in al-Hidayah (4:251).
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage discusses two interconnected issues regarding bequest to a named group. The first part deals with a bequest to a group that can be counted (e.g., 'Bani Fulan'). According to the matn, if the group is countable, both poor and rich members receive a share as individual ownership (tamlik). If the group is uncountable, the bequest becomes a pious act (qurbah) directed to the poor among them. The commentary then defines key terms: 'orphan' (yatim) is one who has lost their caretaker before puberty; after puberty, they are no longer an orphan. 'Armalah' (plural aramil) is a poor person, but the correct definition for a woman is a widow (a woman who had a husband who left or died). The second issue involves whether a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' includes females. The early Hanafi position (first opinion of Abu Hanifa and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that it does include females because the masculine plural can encompass women. Later, Abu Hanifa retracted and said it refers exclusively to males, unless the phrase is a tribal name (like Bani Tamim), in which case it includes both due to lineage. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for the counting issue is the judge's discretion, leaning toward Muhammad's view that more than a hundred is uncountable.

Key Terms
يتيم (yatim): A child who has lost the person who raises them (usually father) before puberty; after puberty, the term no longer applies.
أرملة (armalah): A poor widow (woman who had a husband and he died or left her); the condition of being poor is essential. Not a wealthy woman without a husband.
بنو فلان (banu fulan): The children (descendants) of a specific person; in context of a bequest, it is ambiguous whether it includes females unless it is a tribal name.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later view of Abu Hanifa, if someone makes a bequest to 'Bani Zaid' (where Zaid is an individual, not a tribe), are females included?
A) Yes, always included.
B) No, only males are included.
C) Yes, but only if they are poor.
D) No, unless they constitute the majority.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'Bani Fulan' excludes women unless the name is tribal, as per Abu Hanifa's later view.

Invalidity of Bequest to Mawali Due to Ambiguity
Ruling that a bequest to mawali is invalid because the word is ambiguous

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to 'mawali' and explain the linguistic basis for its invalidity.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'mawali' fails because the word is ambiguous – it cannot cover both master and freed slave.

The word 'mawla' in Arabic carries two opposite meanings: patron (master) and client (freed slave). When a testator says 'I bequeath to my mawali,' the intention is unclear. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that such a bequest is void, and the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is a bequest (wasiyyah) to 'mawali'. What is the Hanafi ruling? It is void (batil).
2
Identify the linguistic reason
The word 'mawla' is homonymous (mushtarak). It can mean either the manumitter or the manumitted. The text states: 'because the word is ambiguous, and it has no general meaning'.
A mushtarak word cannot be used to denote both meanings simultaneously without clarification.
3
Note the absence of a contextual clue (qarinah)
Without a qarinah pointing to one specific meaning, the testator's intent remains unknown. The commentary says: 'no contextual indication points to either one, so it remains unknown in intention'.
If a qarinah existed (e.g., 'my mawali who I manumitted'), the bequest would be valid for that category.
4
Consider the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the term 'mawali' is general and includes all, similar to 'brothers'. The Hanafi response is that 'mawla' is not a general noun but a homonym; the analogy to 'brothers' fails because 'brothers' is not ambiguous.
The thamarah al-khilaf: In Hanafi law, the bequest fails and the property returns to the heirs; in Shafi'i law, it is distributed among all mawali.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Hanafi position: the bequest is void. This is supported by the zahir al-riwayah and confirmed in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطلت الوصية لمواليه فيمن معتقون ومعتقون) ؛ لأنَّ اللفظ (۱) مشترك ، ولا عموم له، ولا قرينة تدلُّ على أحدهما، وفي بعض كتب الشَّافِعِي (1) أن الوصية للكل.
11 ] قوله : لأن اللفظ مشترك... الخ ؛ توضيحه : إن الجهة مختلفة ؛ لأنّ أحدهما : أي المعتق بكسر التاء يسمى مولى النعمة، والثاني : أي المعتق بفتح التاء يسمى منعم عليه، فصار لفظ المولى مشتركاً، ولا عموم له ؛ أي لا يجوز عموم المشترك، بأن يراد به كلا معنييه معاً بإطلاق واحد، ولا قرينة تدل على أحد : أي لا ترجيح البعض على البعض فبقي مجهول المراد، فلا يدرى أنّ المراد أيهما. (1) قوله : للكل ؛ لأن الاسم يتناولهم ؛ لأن كلاً منهم يسمّى مولى، فصار كالأخوة. كذا في «الهداية»).
And the bequest to his mawali is void among those who are manumitted and manumitters. Because the word is ambiguous, and it has no general meaning, and no contextual indication points to either one. And in some books of al-Shafi'i, that the bequest for all. [11] His statement: 'because the word is ambiguous... etc.' Its clarification: Indeed, the aspect is different; because one of them - i.e., the manumitter (with kasra of the ta) is called mawla of favor, and the second - i.e., the manumitted (with fatha of the ta) is called the recipient of favor. So the word 'mawla' became ambiguous, and it has no general meaning, i.e., it is not permissible to apply the general meaning of the ambiguous word, such that both meanings are intended together with a single utterance, and no contextual indication points to either one, i.e., no preference of some over others, so it remains unknown in intention, so it is not known which one is intended. (1) His statement: 'for all'; because the name includes them, because each of them is called mawla, so it becomes like brothers. So in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 625

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a bequest to 'mawali' (plural of mawla) is invalid (batilah) because the term is ambiguous: it can mean both the master (patron) and the freed slave (client). The text explains that since the word is homonymous (mushtarak), it cannot be given a general meaning that includes both simultaneously without a contextual clue (qarinah). Without such clue, the intention of the testator is unknown, so the bequest fails. The Shafi'i school is cited as holding that the bequest is valid for all because each person is called 'mawla', analogous to brothers. However, the Hanafi position rejects this because the word is inherently ambiguous and cannot be taken as general (la 'umuma lah). The relied-upon view is that such a bequest is void.

Key Terms
مولى (mawla): A homonym that can mean either the manumitter (master, patron) or the manumitted (freed slave, client).
قرينة (qarinah): A contextual clue that resolves ambiguity and indicates the intended meaning.
مشترك (mushtarak): A word that has more than one distinct meaning, i.e., a homonym.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the testator cannot have both masters and slaves as beneficiaries.
B) Because the word 'mawali' is ambiguous and lacks a contextual clue to determine the intention.
C) Because the bequest would be against the interest of the heirs.
D) Because it is a bequest to a non-Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school voids a bequest to 'mawali' due to linguistic ambiguity, emphasizing the need for clear intention in wills.

The 'Always' Clause in Bequests: Fruit vs. Wool
Ruling on the effect of 'always' clause in bequests of future produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequeathing future produce when 'always' is added, and apply the distinction between items that can and cannot be contracted upon when non-existent.

Core Idea
Adding 'always' includes future items, but validity depends on whether the item can be contracted non-existent.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a subtle point in bequests (wasiyya). When a testator bequeaths the wool, offspring, or milk of his sheep and adds the word 'always' (abad), does this include future produce? The Hanafi school answers with a critical distinction: the key is whether the item can be validly contracted upon when non-existent. Fruit can, via musaqat; wool cannot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that the default in bequests is to include only what exists at the time of death. The addition of 'always' modifies this intention.
The base rule: bequest covers only existing property unless otherwise indicated.
2
Analyze the effect of 'always'
When 'always' (abad) is attached, it becomes a contextual clue (qarina) that the testator intends future items. However, this does not automatically validate the bequest.
The word 'always' indicates scope but does not override legal restrictions.
3
Distinguish between fruit and wool
Fruit is like ghalla (renewable produce) and can be validly contracted when non-existent (e.g., musaqat). Wool, offspring, and milk are not legally contractible when non-existent.
The authority for fruit's permissibility is the Shariah-validated musaqat contract.
4
Apply qiyas (analogy)
The bequest is analogous to a contract of sale or transfer. Since a musaqat contract on non-existent fruit is valid, the bequest of future fruit with 'always' is valid. No such contract exists for wool, so the bequest is invalid.
The illa (effective cause) is the possibility of a valid contract on the non-existent item.
5
Conclude the ruling
Thus, the bequest of fruit with 'always' is sahih (valid); the bequest of wool, offspring, or milk with 'always' is batil (invalid).
This aligns with the Hanafi position in Zahir al-Riwaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبصوف غنمه، وولدها، ولبنها له ما في وقتِ موتِهِ ضمّ أبدا أو لا، والفرق بين الثَّمرة والغلة والصوف : أنَّ الغلّةَ تطلقُ على الموجود، وعلى ما يوجد مرة بعد أخرى، والثّمرة والصُّوف لا يطلقان إلا على الموجود، إلا أنه إذا ضمّ أبداً صار قرينة دالة على تناول المعدوم، فتصح في الثَّمرة دون الصوف ؛ لأنَّ العقد على الثمرة المعدومة يصح شرعاً كالمساقاة لا على الصوف والولد ونحوهما.
And regarding the wool of his sheep, its offspring, and its milk, [the bequest] is for him what is at the time of his death, whether the condition 'always' is attached or not. The difference between fruit, produce, and wool is that 'produce' applies to what exists and to what comes repeatedly, while 'fruit' and 'wool' only apply to what exists. However, if 'always' is attached, it becomes a context indicating inclusion of non-existent [future items]. So the bequest is valid for fruit but not for wool, because a contract on non-existent fruit is legally valid, like musaqat, but not on wool, offspring, and the like.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of bequeathing future wool, offspring, and milk when the word 'always' is used. The author explains the distinction: when 'always' is attached, it indicates that the intention includes future produce. However, this only works for items that can be validly contracted upon when non-existent, such as fruit in a musaqat contract. Wool, offspring, and milk cannot be contracted upon when non-existent, so the bequest is invalid for them even with 'always'. The key point is that the validity depends on whether the item can be legally subject to a valid contract in its non-existent state.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghallah): Produce that can be obtained repeatedly, used here to distinguish from fruit and wool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fruit is valid, wool is invalid.
B) Both are valid.
C) Both are invalid.
D) Wool is valid, fruit is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of bequeathing future produce with 'always' depends on whether the produce can be legally contracted upon when non-existent – fruit is valid, wool is not.

Inheritance and Bequest of a Church or Synagogue
Ruling on inheritance and bequest of churches and synagogues for non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of a bequest of a church or synagogue and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: valid like waqf; Sahibayn: invalid as disobedience.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a dhimmi bequeath a church or synagogue? Abu Hanifa analogizes it to a waqf and allows it, while his two companions consider it an act of disobedience and declare it invalid. Understanding this difference is crucial for a mufti dealing with non-Muslim communities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) of a church (bi'ah) or synagogue (kanisah) by a dhimmi (Jew or Christian).
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa: the bequest is valid and the building is inheritable. The two companions: invalid because it is a ma'siyah (disobedience).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
He compares it to a waqf, which in his view is inheritable, and argues it is a good deed in the testator's belief.
4
Analyze the companions' dalil
They consider it an act of disobedience in Islamic law, thus the bequest is invalid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
In villages, the difference applies; in cities, it is invalid by consensus. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتورث بيعة وكنيسة جعلنا في الصحة؛ لأنَّ هذا بمنزلة الوقفَ عند أبي حنيفة، والوقف يورث عنده، وأما عندهما : لا؛ لأنَّ هذه معصية فلا تصح. والوصية بجعل أحدهما سمي قوماً، أو لا تصح)، فإن أوصى يهودي أو نصراني أن يجعل القوم مسمين بيعة أو كنيسة تصح، ولقوم غير مسمين تصح عند أبي حنيفة له لا عندهما، فإن الوصية بالمعصية لا تصح، له : أنه قربة في معتقدهم، وهم متروكون على ما يدينون.
And a church or synagogue is inherited; we declare them [valid] in health, because this is like a waqf according to Abu Hanifa, and a waqf is inheritable according to him. But according to the two companions, no, because this is disobedience, so it is invalid. And the bequest by making one of them specified for a people, or not specified—if a Jew or Christian bequeaths that a specified group make it a church or synagogue, it is valid. For an unspecified group, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, not according to the two companions, because a bequest of disobedience is invalid. For him [Abu Hanifa], it is an act of worship in their belief, and they are left to follow their religion.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of a bequest of a church or synagogue. Abu Hanifa analogizes it to a waqf; since waqf is inheritable in his view, the bequest is valid. The two companions argue it is an act of disobedience, thus invalid. For a bequest to a specified group, all agree it is valid. For an unspecified group, Abu Hanifa rules it valid because in their belief it is a good deed; the companions hold it invalid. The text notes that the difference applies in villages; in cities where construction of new churches is prohibited, it is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
بيعة (bi'ah): A church, specifically for Christians, used in the context of bequest.
كنيسة (kanisah): A synagogue or church, for Jews or Christians, used in the same context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions, a bequest of a church is invalid because...
A) It is like a waqf.
B) It is an act of disobedience.
C) The testator is not Muslim.
D) The church cannot be owned.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the relied-upon position is that a bequest for a church or synagogue is valid since non-Muslims are left to their beliefs, though the two companions held it invalid as an act of disobedience.

Bequest for Construction of a Church or Synagogue
Ruling on bequest to make a building into a church or synagogue for specified or unspecified groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the validity of a bequest to build a church or synagogue for specified versus unspecified groups according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Specified group: valid by consensus; unspecified group: valid according to Abu Hanifa, invalid according to Sahibayn.

This passage also deals with a related scenario: a dhimmi bequeaths money to make a building into a church or synagogue. The ruling depends on whether the group of beneficiaries is specified. All agree on validity when specified; when unspecified, Abu Hanifa still allows it while the two companions reject it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A Jew or Christian bequeaths to make something into a church or synagogue for a specified or unspecified group.
2
State the agreed ruling
If the group is specified, the bequest is valid by consensus.
3
State the disputed ruling
If the group is unspecified, Abu Hanifa says valid, companions say invalid.
4
Explain the reasoning
Abu Hanifa: it is a good deed in their belief. Companions: it is disobedience.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if the group is unspecified, the mufta bihi is validity.

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of a bequest of a church or synagogue. Abu Hanifa analogizes it to a waqf; since waqf is inheritable in his view, the bequest is valid. The two companions argue it is an act of disobedience, thus invalid. For a bequest to a specified group, all agree it is valid. For an unspecified group, Abu Hanifa rules it valid because in their belief it is a good deed; the companions hold it invalid. The text notes that the difference applies in villages; in cities where construction of new churches is prohibited, it is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
بيعة (bi'ah): A church, specifically for Christians, used in the context of bequest.
كنيسة (kanisah): A synagogue or church, for Jews or Christians, used in the same context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, a bequest to build a church for an unspecified group is...
A) Invalid like any bequest of disobedience.
B) Valid because it is a good deed in their belief.
C) Valid only if the testator is a Jew.
D) Invalid unless the testator is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a bequest to build a church or synagogue is valid if the beneficiary group is specified; if unspecified, the relied-upon position is validity according to Abu Hanifa.

The Musta'min's Bequest of All Property
Ruling on validity of a musta'min's bequest of all property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a musta'min can bequeath all his property and explain the rationale that absent heirs in Dar al-Harb are treated as deceased.

Core Idea
A musta'min's bequest of all property is valid because his heirs in Dar al-Harb are legally dead.

This lesson examines a specific exception to the general rule that a bequest of more than one-third of one's estate is invalid. The general rule exists to protect the rights of heirs. For a musta'min, however, any heirs residing in Dar al-Harb are not recognized as having claims in Dar al-Islam. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school applies legal reasoning (dalil aqli) to resolve conflicts between property rights and the status of non-Muslims under temporary safe conduct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a musta'min making a will (wasiyya) for all his property. The ruling: it is sahih (valid).
2
Recall the general principle
Normally, a bequest of all property is invalid because it infringes on the rights of heirs (the one-third limit). Recognize that this restriction is based on protecting heirs' shares.
3
Locate the exception for a musta'min
The exception here is that the musta'min has no heir present in Dar al-Islam. His heirs are in Dar al-Harb, and they are legally treated as dead (fi hukm al-amwat). Therefore, no one's rights are violated.
4
Understand the rationale
The impediment (mani) to validity was the existence of heirs with enforceable rights. Since those heirs are absent and legally dead, the impediment is removed. This is a rational deduction (dalil aqli) from the underlying cause (illah).
5
Apply the ruling
If a musta'min has an heir in Dar al-Islam (e.g., a child born there), the one-third restriction applies. If he has no heir locally, the bequest is valid for the entire estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كوصية مستأمن لا وارث له هنا بكلِّ مالِهِ لمسلم أو ذمي، فإنَّ الوصية بكلِّ المال إنما لا تصح لحق الورثة، وأما المستأمن فورثته في دار الحرب، وهم في حكم الأموات، فلا مانع من الصحة.
Like the will of a musta'min who has no heir here [in the land of Islam] for all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi. Indeed, the bequest of all property is invalid only due to the right of heirs. As for the musta'min, his heirs are in the Abode of War, and they are considered as dead, so there is no impediment to validity.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage explains that a musta'min (a non-Muslim with temporary safe conduct) can validly bequeath all his property if he has no heir present in Dar al-Islam. The normal restriction to one-third applies to protect the rights of heirs, but since his heirs are in Dar al-Harb and their rights are not recognized as they are considered legally dead, the bequest is valid for the entire estate. This ruling is based on the principle that the rights of absent heirs in enemy territory are not enforceable.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who has been granted temporary safe conduct (aman) to enter and reside in Dar al-Islam.
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule that is not in a state of peace with the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a musta'min bequeath all his property if he has no heir in Dar al-Islam?
A) Because he is not bound by Islamic laws.
B) Because his heirs in Dar al-Harb are considered dead.
C) Because he is allowed to give all his wealth in charity.
D) Because the Prophet explicitly allowed it.

Key Takeaway
A musta'min with no heir in Dar al-Islam may validly bequeath all his property because the only impediment—the rights of heirs—is absent when those heirs reside in Dar al-Harb and are considered legally dead.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Executor's Recourse After Reclaimed Slave
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on executor's recourse after slave reclamation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the executor's recourse after a reclaimed slave, identify the proofs (taghrir vs. wasiyya limitation), and evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The deceived executor recovers from all assets; the wasiyya executor recovers from one-third.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute where an executor sells a slave under a wasiyya, the price perishes, and the slave is reclaimed. The question is: from what part of the estate can the executor recover the price he had to refund to the buyer? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani offer different answers based on different legal analyses of the nature of the executor's role and liability.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the legal question
Describe the facts: a child inherits a slave; executor sells it under a wasiyya, takes the price, the slave perishes in his hand, then the slave is reclaimed by its true owner. The buyer recovers the price from the executor. The executor now wants to recover that amount from the estate. The question is: from what part of the estate can he recover?
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's initial and final positions
Abu Hanifa first said no recourse because the executor became liable by taking possession. Then he retracted and ruled full recourse from the entire estate due to taghrir (deception by the deceased). Focus on the final position.
The retraction is noted in the text: 'then he retracted to what was mentioned'.
3
State Muhammad's position and his proof
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the executor can only recover from one-third of the estate, because the sale was to execute a wasiyya, and the wasiyya is limited to one-third.
The proof: 'the locus of the wasiyya is one-third'
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's final proof: taghrir (deception)
The deceased misled the executor by claiming the slave was his property. The executor relied on that statement. Therefore, the liability (daman) becomes a debt on the deceased, and debts are paid from the entire estate.
The text cites Imam Qadi Khan for this proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the executor can recover the full price from all assets of the estate. Under Muhammad, only from the one-third portion of the wasiyya, so if the price exceeds one-third, the executor bears the loss.
This affects how estates are administered in such situations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما يرجع في مالِ الطفل وصي باعَ ما أصابه من التركة، وهَلَكَ معه ثمنه فاستحق، والطفل على الورثة بحصته وكان أبو حنيفة الله يقول :أولاً : لا يرجع في التركة ؛ لأنَّه ضَمِنَ بقبضه ، ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إلى ما ذكر "" ، وعند محمد الله يَرْجِعُ في الثُّلث (۳) ؛ لأنَّ محلَّ الوصية الثلث. (كما يرجعُ في مالِ الطفلِ وصي باعَ ما أصابه من التركة، وهَلَكَ معه ثمنه فاستحق، والطفل على الورثَةِ بحصّتِه ) : أي قُسِمَ الميراث فأصابَ الطِّفلُ عبداً ، فباعه الوصي، وقبض ثمنه ، فهَلَكَ العبد في يده، فاستحق العبد، وأخذ المشتري الثَّمَن من الوصي رجعَ الوصي في مالِ الطفل ؛ لأنه عامل له ، ويرجعُ الطِّفلُ على الورثة بنصيبه مما بقي في أيديهم ؛ لأنَّ القسمة قد انتقضت، وصار كان العبد لم يكن. قوله : لا يرجع ؛ أي لا يرجعُ الوصي على أحد ؛ لأنه ضَمِنَ بقبضه ؛ أي لأنه تبين بطلان الوصية باستحقاق الغلام ، ولم يكن عاملاً للورثة، فلا يرجع عليهم بشيء. إلى ما ذكر؛ أي في «المتن» بقوله : ورجع في التركة ؛ أي يرجع في جميع التركة. يرجع في الثلث؛ لأن الرجوع بحكم الوصية ؛ لأن البيع كان لتنفيذ الوصيّة ، فكان حكمه حكم الوصية، ومحل الوصية الثلث. و دليل قول الإمام أنه يرجع - أي الوصي - على الميت على تركته، بحكم أن الميت غيره بقوله : إن هذا ملكي ؛ لأنه لما أمره ببيع عبده وتصدق بثمنه على المساكين كان قائلاً : إنّ هذا العبد ،ملكي، فكان الوصي مغروراً من جهته، فكان ذلك الضمان ديناً على الميت، والدين يقضى من جميع التركة كذا ذكره الإمام قاضي خان له. هذا ما أفاده صاحب «الكفاية». قوله : لأنّ ؛ أي الوصي . عامله؛ أي الطفل. ويرجع الطفل على الورثة بنصيبه : أي الطفل. مما بقي في أيديهم : أي الورثة ؛ لأنَّ القسمة انتقضت باستحقاق ما أصابه ، ، وهو العبد؛ وصار كأنه لم يكن.
As the executor also has recourse in the property of the child — an executor sold what had fallen to the child from the estate, and the price perished with him, then (the slave) was reclaimed, and the child (has recourse) against the heirs for his share. Abu Hanifa said initially: no recourse in the estate because he became liable by taking possession, then he retracted to what was mentioned, and according to Muhammad he has recourse in one-third because the locus of the wasiyya is one-third. (As the executor has recourse in the property of the child — an executor sold what had fallen to the child from the estate, and the price perished with him, then (the slave) was reclaimed, and the child (has recourse) against the heirs for his share): meaning the inheritance was divided, and a slave fell to the child, so the executor sold him and took the price, then the slave perished in his hand, then the slave was reclaimed, and the buyer took the price from the executor; the executor has recourse in the child's property because he is his agent, and the child has recourse against the heirs for his share from what remains in their hands because the division is invalidated and it becomes as if the slave never existed. His statement: 'no recourse' means the executor has no recourse against anyone because he became liable by taking possession; i.e., because the wasiyya is invalidated by the reclamation of the slave, and he was not an agent for the heirs, so he has no recourse against them. 'To what was mentioned' i.e., in the text by his statement: 'and he has recourse in the estate' i.e., he has recourse in all of the estate. 'He has recourse in one-third' because the recourse is by virtue of the wasiyya; because the sale was for executing the wasiyya, so its ruling is the ruling of the wasiyya, and the locus of the wasiyya is one-third. The proof of the Imam's (Abu Hanifa) statement that he (the executor) has recourse against the deceased from his estate, by virtue that the deceased misled him by his statement 'this is my property'; because when he ordered him to sell his slave and give the price in charity to the poor, he was saying 'this slave is my property', so the executor was deceived by him, and that liability became a debt upon the deceased, and the debt is paid from all of the estate, as mentioned by Imam Qadi Khan. This is what the author of al-Kifaya stated. His statement: 'because' i.e., the executor is his (the child's) agent. And the child has recourse against the heirs for his share: i.e., the child. 'from what remains in their hands' i.e., the heirs; because the division is invalidated by the reclamation of what he got, which is the slave, and it becomes as if it never existed.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the executor's (wasi) right of recourse after selling a slave that later turned out to belong to someone else. The scenario: A child inherits a slave from the deceased. The executor, acting under a wasiyya (bequest) to sell the slave and give the price in charity, sells the slave and takes the price. The slave then perishes in the executor's possession, but later the slave is reclaimed by a rightful owner (istihqaq). The buyer recovers the price from the executor. Now the executor seeks to recover the price from the child's property or from the heirs. The dispute: Abu Hanifa initially held that the executor has no recourse at all because he became liable (damin) by taking possession of the price. However, he later retracted and ruled that the executor has recourse against the deceased's entire estate, because the deceased misled him by claiming the slave was his property, making the executor a misled party (maghrur). Thus, the liability becomes a debt on the deceased, payable from all the estate. Muhammad al-Shaybani, on the other hand, holds that the executor's recourse is limited to one-third of the estate, because the sale was to execute the wasiyya, and the wasiyya is valid only up to one-third. The narrator explains that the child also has recourse against the other heirs for his share from the remaining estate, because the original division is invalidated by the reclamation. The passage emphasizes the principles of liability (daman), deception (taghrir), and the limitation of wasiyya to one-third.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): An executor appointed by the deceased or by the qadi to manage the estate and execute wasiyya.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Reclamation of property by rightful owner, invalidating prior sale.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss of property; here the executor becomes liable for the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final position of Abu Hanifa, from what part of the estate does the executor have recourse after the slave is reclaimed?
A) Only from the one-third of the wasiyya
B) From the entire estate
C) Only from the minor's share
D) No recourse at all

Key Takeaway
The executor's recourse after a reclaimed slave is a debt on the entire estate (Abu Hanifa) or limited to one-third (Muhammad), depending on whether the sale is attributed to taghrir or to the wasiyya.
